Method of Learning
beginner
6 min
The Three Methods of Usul al-Fiqh Composition
Classification of usul composition methods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three methods of usul al-fiqh composition and identify which method defines Muslim al-Thubut.

Core Idea
Usul al-Fiqh composition follows three methods: the theologians' method, the jurists' method, and their combination.

This passage explains why Usul al-Fiqh is essential: finite texts must address infinite human events. It then categorises the two dominant methodologies for writing usul works—the theologian method (mutakallimin) and the jurist method (fuqaha)—and introduces a third combined method. Understanding this classification helps you situate any usul text you study, especially the Hanafi school's reliance on the combined approach in works like Muslim al-Thubut.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem that Usul al-Fiqh solves
The passage states that divine texts are limited while human events are unlimited, creating a need for principles to derive rulings.
This is the foundational justification for usul.
2
List the three methods of composition
Name them from the passage: Tariqat al-Mutakallimin, Tariqat al-Fuqaha, and the combined method.
These are the three approaches to writing usul works.
3
Distinguish the first two methods
Mutakallimin: based on logical/theological premises, independent of fiqh branches. Fuqaha: derived from existing fiqh rulings of the imams, ensuring principles conform to the madhhab.
The key difference is the source of principles.
4
Identify the combined method and its key work
The combined method integrates both. Muslim al-Thubut by Muhibb Allah al-Bahari is a prime example.
Al-Bahari states his book contains both methods.
5
Recognise the significance of combined works for Hanafi usul
Combined works bridge the Shafi'i/mutakallimun style with the Hanafi/fuqaha style, making them comprehensive yet challenging.
Most advanced Hanafi usul texts follow this combined approach.

فللمسلّم حواش وشروح ، وعليه تعليقات قديمة وجديدة ، ومن تعليقاته الجديدة في عصرنا وشروحه العجيبة النادرة أمالي“ شيخ الأصول وإمام المعقول الأستاذ الكبير الشيخ خان بهادر المارتونگى السواتي، ( المتوفى ١٩٧٦هـ) رحمه
الله رحمة واسعة ، وكان الأمالي بلغة شعبه (البشتو) وتلك الأمالي من أسهل تعليقاته، وأجمعها، وأنفعها، وأكثرها حلاً لمغلقات الكتاب ومعقداته ، فإنّ البهاري - بما أن كتابه جامع بين الطريقتين المعروفتين - قد استخدم الأسلوب الكلامي والمنطقي والبلاغي، مغيّرا أكثر كلام الأصوليين في تعريفاته، وتعبيراته ، فصار كتابه من أصعب
(1) اقتبست "المقدمة" بتغيير يسير إلى هنا من أنوار مقدمة "تعليق " فضيلة الدكتور عبدالرحيم فيروز الهروي على كتاب "تقويم الأصول وأدلة الشرع".
Izalat al-Rahbut an Mushkilat Muslim al-Thubut. Religious sciences. 6. This is because the sacred texts of the Book and Sunnah, according to what His wisdom necessitated, are limited and confined, while the necessities of life and the needs of people are unlimited and without end. For it is in the nature of events that they are not eternal and unchanging; rather, change and renewal are among their characteristics. Thus, events and occurrences may arise in human society that were not known yesterday, and conditions and situations continue to change, and new events occur that require scholars to issue an appropriate legal ruling for them and to explain their rulings from the principles of the texts and the objectives of Shariah. If they stood before those events with folded hands, it would necessitate judging Islamic law as stagnant, lagging behind in fulfilling people's needs, and insufficient to meet the needs of human societies at various levels—far be it from that. So to address this problem, it is necessary to resort to Usul al-Fiqh and practice its principles in order to face life with full strength, courage, and stability, by applying the rulings of our eternal Shariah that is sufficient for every new development and change, and for every country and era. Our sincere previous scholars fulfilled this legal need with their established and chosen methodologies, and they continued night and day until they were able to prepare for us a great heritage and abundant oceans, from which by diving one can extract luminous, refined pearls worthy of admiration. Among that heritage or pearls is the book 'al-Muslim' by the author of al-Sullam al-Nazar, the theologian, philosopher, logician, and usuli, Muhibb Allah al-Bahari al-Hindi (d. 1119 AH). This book has a wonderful style and strange expression, coming in theological terms and logical expressions. He chose conciseness and preferred inimitability, and began his book with truth and metaphor, real and metaphorical existence. Nonetheless, it is among the books authored on the combination of the two prevalent methods. For it is well-known that scholars of usul and authors of Usul al-Fiqh have three methods of composition: 1. The method of the theologians: This is the method whose proponents focus on refining issues and establishing principles based on logical and theological foundations, and presenting evidences from those foundations, stripped of fiqh sub-branches. Rather, their approach in this is like that of the theologians, and therefore this method is called the method of the theologians. From this, 'Ubayd Allah al-Bukhari says in the introduction to his 'Tawdih': 'Its foundation is on rational principles.' 2. The method of the jurists: This is the method whose proponents are concerned with fiqh sub-branches and particulars, and they devote themselves to serving them, by establishing usul principles according to what has been transmitted from their imams of fiqh branches. They reckon that those principles are what the imams observed when they derived those branches from their foundations. So if they find a principle that contradicts those established branches, they strive to shape it in a way that suits those principles; hence this method is called the method of the jurists or the Hanafi method. 3. There is a third method: Combining the first two methods. So 'al-Muslim' which is known as Muslim al-Thubut is from the third category, as the author himself says: 'My book contains the Hanafi method (the jurists' method) and the Shafi'i method (the theologians' method).' (1) Among the books combining the two methods are al-Tawdih (commentary on al-Tanqih) by 'Ubayd Allah al-Bukhari and its gloss al-Talwih by al-Taftazani, and 'Tahrir al-Usul' by Ibn al-Humam and its commentary 'al-Taqrir wa al-Tahbir' by Ibn Amir al-Hajj, and 'Badi' al-Nizam' by al-Sa'ati. So al-Muslim has glosses and commentaries, and old and new annotations. Among its new annotations in our time and its amazing rare commentaries is 'al-Amali' by the Sheikh of Usul and Imam of Rational Sciences, the great professor Sheikh Khan Bahadur al-Martunghawi al-Suwati (d. 1976 AH), may Allah have vast mercy on him. Al-Amali was in the language of his people (Pashto), and those Amali are among his easiest annotations, most comprehensive, most beneficial, and most resolving of the book's obscurities and intricacies. For al-Bahari—since his book combines the two well-known methods—used the theological, logical, and rhetorical style, changing most of the usuli scholars' expressions in his definitions and terms, making his book one of the most difficult.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage is an opening discussion on the necessity of Usul al-Fiqh and the classification of methods of composition in this field. The author begins by explaining why Usul al-Fiqh is needed: the divine texts are finite while human events are infinite, so scholars must derive rulings using principles from the texts and objectives of Shariah. Without this, Islamic law would be seen as insufficient. The author then credits earlier scholars for preserving this heritage. He introduces Muhibb Allah al-Bahari's 'Muslim al-Thubut' as a book that combines two prevalent methods of usul writing. He then defines the three methods: (1) The method of the mutakallimun (theologians), which relies on logical and theological premises to establish usul principles, independent of fiqh branches, akin to the approach of 'ilm al-kalam. (2) The method of the fuqaha (jurists), which builds usul principles from the existing fiqh rulings transmitted from the imams, ensuring that principles conform to the madhhab's established branches. This is associated with the Hanafi school. (3) The combined method, which integrates both approaches. 'Muslim al-Thubut' is placed in this third category, as al-Bahari himself states. The passage then lists other well-known combined works: 'al-Tawdih' by 'Ubayd Allah al-Bukhari (commentary on 'al-Tanqih'), its gloss 'al-Talwih' by al-Taftazani, 'Tahrir al-Usul' by Ibn al-Humam with 'al-Taqrir wa al-Tahbir' by Ibn Amir al-Hajj, and 'Badi' al-Nizam' by al-Sa'ati. Finally, the author praises a recent commentary on 'Muslim al-Thubut' called 'al-Amali' by Sheikh Khan Bahadur al-Martunghawi al-Suwati, written in Pashto, which he considers the most clear and beneficial for resolving the book's difficulties. He notes that al-Bahari's book is challenging because it combines both methods and uses theological, logical, and rhetorical terminology that differs from standard usul expressions.

Key Terms
طريقة المتكلمين (Tariqat al-Mutakallimin): A method of usul al-fiqh composition that focuses on establishing principles based on logical and theological foundations, independent of specific fiqh branches.
طريقة الفقهاء (Tariqat al-Fuqaha): A method of usul al-fiqh composition that derives principles from the established fiqh rulings of the imams, ensuring that principles conform to the madhhab's branches.
مسلم الثبوت (Muslim al-Thubut): A book on usul al-fiqh by Muhibb Allah al-Bahari that combines the methods of the mutakallimin and the fuqaha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what are the three methods of composition in Usul al-Fiqh?
A) The method of the Fuqaha, the method of the Mutakallimin, and the method of the Sufis.
B) The method of the Mutakallimin, the method of the Fuqaha, and a combined method.
C) The method of the Hanafis, the method of the Shafi'is, and the method of the Malikis.
D) The method of the early scholars, the method of the later scholars, and the method of the modern scholars.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-Fiqh composition methods vary: theologians abstract, jurists ground in fiqh, and combined works like Muslim al-Thubut integrate both.

Method of Learning
beginner
6 min
The Method of the Mutakallimin in Usul al-Fiqh
Describes the mutakallimin method in usul al-fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the characteristics of the mutakallimin method and explain why it is associated with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Mutakallimin build usul on rational principles, independent of juristic branches.

In the preface of his commentary, the author distinguishes two main schools of thought in usul al-fiqh. The first is the method of the mutakallimin, or theologians, who base their usul on logic and rational deduction rather than on the specific rulings of the imams. This approach is characteristic of the Shafi'i school and is often contrasted with the Hanafi method grounded in furu'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main methods
Read the first part of the passage which introduces three methods. Focus on the first method: the method of the mutakallimin.
The text says it is 'stripped of juristic branches' and 'upon rational principles'.
2
Understand the rational basis
Note that the mutakallimin method is described as being based on rational principles (قواعد المعقول), similar to the science of kalam (dialectical theology).
This is why it is called 'the method of the theologians'.
3
Recognize the Shafi'i association
The text implies this method is typically used by the Shafi'i school. The author later contrasts it with the Hanafi method.
Al-Ghazali's al-Mustasfa is a classic example of this method.

Removing the Fear from the Difficulties of Musallam al-Thubut: stripped of juristic branches, rather their status in that is the status of theologians, and therefore that method is called the method of the theologians. From that, 'Ubayd Allah al-Bukhari says in the introduction of his al-Tawdih: "And its foundation is upon rational principles." 2. The Method of the Jurists: It is the method whose proponents care about juristic branches and particulars, and they turn to serve them, by establishing the principles of usul according to what is transmitted from their imams of juristic furu', calculating that those principles are what the imams observed when they derived those furu' from their usul, until if they find a principle that contradicts those established furu', they strive to shape it in a way that suits those principles; hence this method is called the method of the jurists or the Hanafi method. 3. And here is a third method: combining the first two methods. So 'al-Musallam' which is known as Musallam al-Thubut is from the third section, as al-Muhibb himself says: "My book contains the Hanafi method (method of the jurists) and the Shafi'i method (method of the theologians)." Among the books that combine the two methods are al-Tawdih, the commentary on al-Tanqih by 'Ubayd Allah al-Bukhari, and its gloss al-Talwih by al-Taftazani, and Tahrir al-Usul by Ibn al-Humam, and its commentary al-Taqrir wa al-Tahbir by Ibn Amir al-Hajj, and Badi' al-Nizam by al-Sa'ati. Among its new annotations in our time and its rare wonderful commentaries are Amali by Shaykh al-Usul and Imam al-Ma'qul the great professor Shaykh Khan Bahadur al-Martunghi al-Sawati (d. 1976 AH), may Allah have abundant mercy on him. And the Amali was in the language of his people (Pashto), and those Amali are among his easiest, most comprehensive, most beneficial annotations, and most solving of the book's difficulties and complexities. Indeed, al-Bihari - since his book combines the two known methods - used the dialectical, logical, and rhetorical style, changing most of the speech of the usuliyyun in his definitions and expressions, so his book became one of the most difficult books of usul al-fiqh, until students, even teachers, were unable to understand most of its phrases and solve its general problems except those deeply rooted in usul and the sciences that the author used in composing his book. From this aspect, the dictation of our most noble professor became among the best Amali and finest commentaries in circulation. And since I had studied under the Shaykh 'al-Marsad al-Awwal' from Sharh al-Mawaqif by al-Sayyid al-Jurjani, with his difficult concise annotations by al-Sayyid al-Zahid al-Harawi in the year 1392 AH at Dar al-Ulum al-Haqqaniyya (Sidu Sharif) corresponding to 1969 CE, I desired to benefit from the Shaykh's Amali and to benefit the students of usul, and then I rolled up my sleeves with determination to explain 'Musallam al-Thubut' with a new, easy, accessible explanation, making the Shaykh's dictations the basis of this work, and I began the explanation with the help and success of Allah. The sources from which I derived: 1. The annotation of the author himself who at the end of his speech uses the word 'minhu' instead of 'lahu', because in reference it is said: 'this book is for so-and-so' or 'this article is for so-and-so', and it is not said 'from so-and-so'. 2. al-Tawdih, the commentary on al-Tanqih, both by 'Ubayd Allah al-Bukhari. 3. The gloss 'al-Talwih 'ala al-Tawdih' by al-Taftazani the Allamah. 4. The commentary of 'Abd al-Haqq al-Khayrabadi on 'al-Muslim'. 5. Kashf al-Mubham 'an al-Muslim. 6. Fawatih al-Rahmut fi Sharh Musallam al-Thubut by Bahr al-Ulum al-Lakhnawi. 7. Taqwim Usul al-Fiqh wa Ta'yin Adillat al-Shar' by Imam Abi Zayd al-Dabusi. 8. Amali al-Shaykh Khan Bahadur al-Martunghi. 9. Tahrir al-Usul by Ibn al-Humam, author of Fath al-Qadir, commentary on Hidaya al-Marghinani. 10. Its commentary al-Taqrir wa al-Tahbir by Ibn Amir al-Hajj. 11. Sullum al-Ulum by the author of 'al-Muslim'.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage is the preface of the author, explaining the methodological background of Musallam al-Thubut and his own approach in writing this commentary. He distinguishes two major methods in usul al-fiqh: (1) The method of the mutakallimun (theologians), which focuses on rational principles and theoretical foundations independent of juristic branches; (2) The method of the fuqaha (jurists), which derives usul principles from the established furu' of the imams, especially the Hanafi school. Then he mentions a third method that combines both, which is the approach of Musallam al-Thubut by Muhammad al-Bihari. The author notes that al-Bihari's work is difficult because it incorporates dialectical, logical, and rhetorical styles, altering traditional usul definitions and expressions. He then states his intention to write an easy commentary based on the Amali of his teacher Shaykh Khan Bahadur al-Martunghi, listing his sources, including key Hanafi usul works like al-Tawdih, al-Talwih, Tahrir al-Usul, etc. This front matter sets the stage for a commentary that aims to unlock the complexities of Musallam al-Thubut.

Key Terms
طريقة المتكلمين (tariqat al-mutakallimin): The method of theologians in usul al-fiqh that focuses on rational principles and theoretical foundations, independent of juristic branches.
قواعد المعقول (qawa'id al-ma'qul): Rational principles, as opposed to transmitted (naqli) sources; the foundation of the mutakallimin method.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis of the mutakallimin method?
A) The juristic branches of the Hanafi imams
B) Rational principles
C) The six authentic hadith collections
D) The consensus of the early Muslims

Key Takeaway
The mutakallimin method in usul al-fiqh is built on rational principles, not on the furu' of the imams, and is characteristic of the Shafi'i school.

Method of Learning
beginner
6 min
The Method of the Fuqaha in Usul al-Fiqh
Describes the fuqaha method in usul al-fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the fuqaha method and how it derives usul from the furu' of the Hanafi imams.

Core Idea
Fuqaha method derives usul principles from the established furu' of the Hanafi imams.

The second major method in usul al-fiqh is the method of the fuqaha (jurists), which is characteristic of the Hanafi school. Unlike the mutakallimin, this method prioritizes the practical rulings (furu') of the Hanafi imams and derives usul principles from them. This approach ensures that the principles of usul are consistent with the established fiqh of the school.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of the fuqaha method
In the passage, the fuqaha method is described as caring about 'juristic branches and particulars' and serving them.
The method is named after the jurists (fuqaha), specifically the Hanafi fuqaha.
2
Understand the derivation process
The fuqaha establish usul principles based on what is transmitted from their imams in terms of furu'. They assume that these furu' were derived from certain usul, and they formulate those usul to match the furu'.
If a potential usul principle contradicts the established furu', they adjust it to fit.
3
Note the Hanafi identity
The text explicitly calls this 'the method of the jurists or the Hanafi method' (طريقة الفقهاء أو طريقة الحنيفة).
This method is the dominant approach in the Hanafi madhhab.

From that, 'Ubayd Allah al-Bukhari says in the introduction of his al-Tawdih: "And its foundation is upon rational principles." 2. The Method of the Jurists: It is the method whose proponents care about juristic branches and particulars, and they turn to serve them, by establishing the principles of usul according to what is transmitted from their imams of juristic furu', calculating that those principles are what the imams observed when they derived those furu' from their usul, until if they find a principle that contradicts those established furu', they strive to shape it in a way that suits those principles; hence this method is called the method of the jurists or the Hanafi method. 3. And here is a third method: combining the first two methods. The Combined Method and Musallam al-Thubut
Describes the combined method and the difficulty of Musallam al-Thubut.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the combined method in usul al-fiqh and identify why Musallam al-Thubut is considered a bridging text.

Core Idea
Musallam al-Thubut combines mutakallimin and fuqaha methods, making it both comprehensive and difficult.

The passage mentions a third method that combines the two previous approaches. This is the method used by Muhammad al-Bihari in his work 'Musallam al-Thubut'. The author notes that al-Bihari used a dialectical, logical, and rhetorical style, changing traditional definitions, which made the book very difficult. The combined method aims to integrate rational principles with the juristic tradition, and understanding it is key to unlocking many usul works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the third method
The text says: 'And here is a third method: combining the first two methods.'
This method is used in Musallam al-Thubut.
2
Note the difficulty of the combined approach
Al-Bihari used a dialectical (kalami) and logical style, altering standard usul definitions. This made his book very difficult.
The author describes it as 'one of the most difficult books of usul al-fiqh'.
3
Recognize the value of commentary
The author of this preface relies on the Amali of his teacher to explain Musallam, indicating the need for expert guidance.
Other combined books include al-Tawdih, al-Talwih, Tahrir al-Usul, etc.

- شرحه التقرير والتحبير " لابن أمير الحاج.
-۱۱ سلّم العلوم لصاحب "المسلم".
Removing the Fear from the Difficulties of Musallam al-Thubut: stripped of juristic branches, rather their status in that is the status of theologians, and therefore that method is called the method of the theologians. From that, 'Ubayd Allah al-Bukhari says in the introduction of his al-Tawdih: "And its foundation is upon rational principles." 2. The Method of the Jurists: It is the method whose proponents care about juristic branches and particulars, and they turn to serve them, by establishing the principles of usul according to what is transmitted from their imams of juristic furu', calculating that those principles are what the imams observed when they derived those furu' from their usul, until if they find a principle that contradicts those established furu', they strive to shape it in a way that suits those principles; hence this method is called the method of the jurists or the Hanafi method. 3. And here is a third method: combining the first two methods. So 'al-Musallam' which is known as Musallam al-Thubut is from the third section, as al-Muhibb himself says: "My book contains the Hanafi method (method of the jurists) and the Shafi'i method (method of the theologians)." Among the books that combine the two methods are al-Tawdih, the commentary on al-Tanqih by 'Ubayd Allah al-Bukhari, and its gloss al-Talwih by al-Taftazani, and Tahrir al-Usul by Ibn al-Humam, and its commentary al-Taqrir wa al-Tahbir by Ibn Amir al-Hajj, and Badi' al-Nizam by al-Sa'ati. Musallam has glosses and commentaries, and old and new annotations. Among its new annotations in our time and its rare wonderful commentaries are Amali by Shaykh al-Usul and Imam al-Ma'qul the great professor Shaykh Khan Bahadur al-Martunghi al-Sawati (d. 1976 AH), may Allah have abundant mercy on him. And the Amali was in the language of his people (Pashto), and those Amali are among his easiest, most comprehensive, most beneficial annotations, and most solving of the book's difficulties and complexities. Indeed, al-Bihari - since his book combines the two known methods - used the dialectical, logical, and rhetorical style, changing most of the speech of the usuliyyun in his definitions and expressions, so his book became one of the most difficult books of usul al-fiqh, until students, even teachers, were unable to understand most of its phrases and solve its general problems except those deeply rooted in usul and the sciences that the author used in composing his book. From this aspect, the dictation of our most noble professor became among the best Amali and finest commentaries in circulation. And since I had studied under the Shaykh 'al-Marsad al-Awwal' from Sharh al-Mawaqif by al-Sayyid al-Jurjani, with his difficult concise annotations by al-Sayyid al-Zahid al-Harawi in the year 1392 AH at Dar al-Ulum al-Haqqaniyya (Sidu Sharif) corresponding to 1969 CE, I desired to benefit from the Shaykh's Amali and to benefit the students of usul, and then I rolled up my sleeves with determination to explain 'Musallam al-Thubut' with a new, easy, accessible explanation, making the Shaykh's dictations the basis of this work, and I began the explanation with the help and success of Allah. The sources from which I derived: 1. The annotation of the author himself who at the end of his speech uses the word 'minhu' instead of 'lahu', because in reference it is said: 'this book is for so-and-so' or 'this article is for so-and-so', and it is not said 'from so-and-so'. 2. al-Tawdih, the commentary on al-Tanqih, both by 'Ubayd Allah al-Bukhari. 3. The gloss 'al-Talwih 'ala al-Tawdih' by al-Taftazani the Allamah. 4. The commentary of 'Abd al-Haqq al-Khayrabadi on 'al-Muslim'. 5. Kashf al-Mubham 'an al-Muslim. 6. Fawatih al-Rahmut fi Sharh Musallam al-Thubut by Bahr al-Ulum al-Lakhnawi. 7. Taqwim Usul al-Fiqh wa Ta'yin Adillat al-Shar' by Imam Abi Zayd al-Dabusi. 8. Amali al-Shaykh Khan Bahadur al-Martunghi. 9. Tahrir al-Usul by Ibn al-Humam, author of Fath al-Qadir, commentary on Hidaya al-Marghinani. 10. Its commentary al-Taqrir wa al-Tahbir by Ibn Amir al-Hajj. 11. Sullum al-Ulum by the author of 'al-Muslim'.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage is the preface of the author, explaining the methodological background of Musallam al-Thubut and his own approach in writing this commentary. He distinguishes two major methods in usul al-fiqh: (1) The method of the mutakallimun (theologians), which focuses on rational principles and theoretical foundations independent of juristic branches; (2) The method of the fuqaha (jurists), which derives usul principles from the established furu' of the imams, especially the Hanafi school. Then he mentions a third method that combines both, which is the approach of Musallam al-Thubut by Muhammad al-Bihari. The author notes that al-Bihari's work is difficult because it incorporates dialectical, logical, and rhetorical styles, altering traditional usul definitions and expressions. He then states his intention to write an easy commentary based on the Amali of his teacher Shaykh Khan Bahadur al-Martunghi, listing his sources, including key Hanafi usul works like al-Tawdih, al-Talwih, Tahrir al-Usul, etc. This front matter sets the stage for a commentary that aims to unlock the complexities of Musallam al-Thubut.

Key Terms
الطريقة الجامعة (al-tariqat al-jami'a): The combined method that integrates the mutakallimin (theologians) and fuqaha (jurists) approaches in usul al-fiqh.
مسلم الثبوت (musallam al-thubut): A foundational text in Hanafi usul al-fiqh by Muhammad al-Bihari, known for combining the mutakallimin and fuqaha methods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Musallam al-Thubut combines the mutakallimin and fuqaha methods, and its difficulty arises from al-Bihari's innovative terminology and integration of both approaches.

The Prophet as Completer of Rulings through the Middle Path
Explains the phrase 'المتمم للحكم بالطريق الأمم' as praise of the Prophet

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two complementary interpretations of the phrase 'المتمم للحكم بالطريق الأمم' and explain how each is supported by Quranic and Hadith evidence.

Core Idea
The Prophet perfected both external rulings and inner character through the balanced middle path.

This passage unpacks a praise-laden phrase from a classical usul text. The author shows that the Prophet's completion of rulings is not a mere repetition but a perfection of the middle path—balancing extremes of prior laws and embodying the Quranic character. Understanding this helps grasp the comprehensive nature of prophetic mission as a source of law and ethics.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base phrase and its grammatical structure
Locate the phrase 'المتمم للحكم بالطريق الأمم' in the source. Note that 'متمم' is an intensive form (مفعِّل) indicating completion and 'الحكم' is plural of حكمة. 'بالطريق الأمم' specifies the means: the most balanced path.
The phrase is a praise (صفة مادحة) for the word 'محمد'.
2
Recognize the two interpretations offered
The author first interprets completion of shar'i rulings (beliefs, ethics, worship, transactions, policies) without excess/deficiency. Then offers a second interpretation: completion of good morals (مكارم الأخلاق) in a moderate manner. Both highlight the middle path.
These are not contradictory but complementary dimensions of the Prophet's mission.
3
Trace the dalil for each interpretation
For the first interpretation, the author cites Quran 5:3 ('Today I have perfected for you your religion...'). For the second, the hadith 'I was sent to perfect noble character traits' and Quran 68:4 ('Indeed, you are upon an excellent character') and 17:39 ('That is from the wisdom your Lord has revealed to you').
The term 'wisdom' (حكمة) in 17:39 links back to the phrase's 'الحكم'.
4
Synthesize the overall message
The Prophet's completion is both legislative (the middle path in rulings) and moral (embodying the Quran). This dual perfection distinguishes Islam from earlier religions, which had either excess (Moses) or deficiency (Jesus) in subsidiary branches.
The middle path is a distinguishing feature of Islam, fitting for a diverse and enduring community.

Source Text

His saying: 'The completer of the rulings through the most balanced path' is a praise attribute for the word 'Muhammad', i.e., the perfecter of the rulings (plural of wisdom which are the shar'i matters of beliefs, ethics, acts of worship, transactions, and policies that Allah revealed in His book, and there is no excess nor deficiency in his teaching and perfecting them, but rather through the middle path which is among the distinguishing features of Islam. The fundamentals of beliefs in previous laws, although they were complete and perfect, but the subsidiary branches of rulings were not in previous religions (according to the author's claim) upon the middle path, rather there was excess or deficiency. Thus the rulings of the religion of Moses, peace be upon him, (due to the harshness and transgression of the Children of Israel) had excess and difficulties; as for the rulings of the religion of Jesus, peace be upon him, there was deficiency, facilitation, and alleviation, because his nation (the Children of Israel in his time) did not have the difficulty and severity like the previous ones, so he alleviated and made easy for them in rulings. And since his nation (the community) was a great (numerous) nation remaining until the Day of Resurrection, and they had different natures and thoughts and diverse aptitudes, Allah chose for them a middle path between making difficult and excess and deficiency. Thus dissection of the expression in this manner is in agreement with His saying: 'Today I have perfected for you your religion and completed My favor upon you and have chosen for you Islam as your religion' (Quran 5:3). And it is possible that the meaning of the expression is as follows: That he perfected good morals in a moderate manner free from excess and deficiency, in agreement with his saying, peace be upon him: 'I was sent to perfect noble character traits.' And the addition of 'noble' to 'character traits' is of the type of adding an adjective to the described. Thus the Prophet taught people aspects of character that no one knew before him. Allah said describing His Messenger: 'And indeed, you are upon an excellent character' (Quran 68:4), indicating that His Prophet is a fountain of good morals and great qualities. And the great character is that which the wise Quran brought as guidance for mankind. And when A'isha, may Allah be pleased with her, was asked about the character of the Prophet, peace be upon him, she said: 'His character was the Quran.' So adhering to the correct beliefs upon which Ahl al-Sunnah wal-Jama'ah have agreed, and obeying the commands, and avoiding the prohibitions that came in the Quran and Sunnah, these are the good morals and noble character traits. Indeed, Allah mentioned in Surah al-Isra' various commands, prohibitions, and morals, then said: 'That is from the wisdom your Lord has revealed to you' (Quran 17:39). So Allah called all of them wisdom. And it is not far that the author's saying 'the completer of the rulings' refers to what is in this verse. And wisdom is the head and foundation of human morals. And in the terminology of the Sufis, embodying noble character traits is called 'maqam' (station), and its plural...
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed commentary on the phrase 'المتمم للحكم بالطريق الأمم' (the completer of rulings through the most balanced path), which is a praise of Prophet Muhammad. The author explains that 'الحكم' (plural of حكمة) refers to all religious sciences: beliefs, ethics, worship, transactions, and policies revealed by Allah. The Prophet perfected these without excess or deficiency, following the middle path, which is a hallmark of Islam. The author contrasts this with previous religions: the law of Moses had excess due to the harshness of the Israelites, while the law of Jesus was overly lenient. The Muslim community, being diverse and permanent until the Day of Judgment, was given a balanced law. This is supported by Quran 5:3. Then the author presents an alternative interpretation: the Prophet perfected good morals in a moderate way, citing the hadith 'I was sent to perfect noble character traits' and Quran 68:4. The character of the Prophet was the Quran itself. Thus, the completion of rulings includes both the external laws and the internal moral character. The author connects this to the term 'wisdom' in Quran 17:39, which encompasses all good morals and commands. This shows the comprehensive nature of the Prophet's mission.

Key Terms
الحكم (al-hikam): Plural of hikma (wisdom); here meaning the shar'i rulings covering beliefs, ethics, worship, transactions, and policies.
الطريق الأمم (al-tariq al-amam): The most balanced/middle path, free from excess (ifrat) and deficiency (tafrit).
مكارم الأخلاق (makarim al-akhlaq): Noble character traits; the moral perfection that the Prophet came to complete.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Quran 17:39 and 68:4 together

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's mission perfected both external shar'i rulings and internal character through a balanced middle path, distinct from the extremes of previous religions.

Method of Learning

Two Types of Proofs for the Excellence of Usul al-Fiqh
Defines two logical proofs and applies them to usul al-fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define burhan limmi and burhan inni, distinguish them with examples, and apply both to establish the excellence of usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh is proven excellent by causal proof (limmi) as its knowledge causes fiqh understanding, and by evidential proof (inni) through its vast literature.

This passage introduces two fundamental types of logical proofs used in Islamic sciences: causal proof (burhan limmi) and evidential proof (burhan inni). Understanding these will sharpen your ability to reason about the status of any Islamic discipline. The author then applies them to demonstrate why usul al-fiqh is the noblest science – both as a cause for deriving fiqh and as evidenced by the great works written on it.

Guided Path
1
Define burhan limmi and burhan inni
Read the definitions: burhan limmi infers effect from cause; burhan inni infers cause from effect. Note the examples (God and universe, sun and day).
These are not unique to Hanafis but standard in usul.
2
Identify the limmi argument for usul al-fiqh
The author argues that profound knowledge (tabahhur) in usul al-fiqh is the cause (illa) for understanding fiqh. Since fiqh is derived from Quran and Sunnah, usul is the means.
This is a causal argument: usul → fiqh understanding.
3
Identify the inni argument for usul al-fiqh
The existence of many books, treatises, and lectures praising usul al-fiqh are effects that indicate its honor. These are burhan inni.
Effects (books) prove the cause (excellence).
4
Analyze the classification of usul books
The author categorizes usul works into Hanafi method, Shafi'i method, and mixed. This diversity shows widespread engagement, strengthening the inni proof.
Examples: Usul al-Bazdawi (Hanafi), al-Mustasfa (Shafi'i), al-Tahrir (mixed).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرف علم أصول الفقه وفضله بالبراهين اللمية، وهنا إثبات شرفه وفضله بالبراهين الإنية. فالبرهان اللمّى هو الاستدلال بالعلة للوصول إلى المعلول كالاستدلال بوجود الله تعالى للوصول الى وجود الكون ، أو الاستدلال بطلوع الشمس للوصول إلى وجود النهار . والبرهان الإنّى : هو الاستدلال بالمعلول للوصول إلى العلة كا لاستدلال بوجود الكون للوصول إلى وجود الله تعالى، أو كا لاستدلال بوجود النهار للوصول إلى طلوع الشمس . وقد علم من السابق أن أخذ الفقه من الكتاب والسنة لا يكون سهلاً وممكناً بالإمكان الواقعي إلا بعد التبخر في مبادى الفقه ومن مباديه علم أصول الفقه فالتبحر والتحذق في أصول الفقه علّة لفهم الفقه والأحكام، وإنما يكون التبحر بأخذها من منابعها الأصلية الكتاب والسنة، فصار التبحر في أصول الفقه علة لادراك مسائل الفقه ، فهذا هو البرهان اللمى وأما تاليف الرّسائل والخطب في مدحه (مدح) أصول الفقه)، وكذا تصنيف الكتب العظيمة و المباحث الدقيقة في أصول الفقه وقواعده، فأمارات وآثار دالة و براهين إنّية على شرفه. يعنى إيذاعة أصحاب الجرائدِ الرّسائل والجرائد في مدحه ، وكذا إلقاء الخطباء محاضراتهم حول أهميته وضرورته للأمة دليل واضح يثبت منه شرف علم أصول الفقه وفضله، كما أنْ تاليف كتب عظيمة دقيقة المباحث بأساليبها المختلفة دليل إني على شرفه وفضله من بين العلوم الاسلامية . والتَنوين في كتب للتعظيم والتكثير ، أي ألفت كتب عظيمة وكثيرة، والمراد بهذه الكتب كتب أصول الفقه للمتقدمين مثل أصول البزدوى وأصول السرخسى ومستصفي الغزالى ومختصر ابن الحاجب ، فإن بعضها على طريقة الحنفية وبعضها على طريقة الشافعية (كما أشار المصنف إلى هاتين الطريقتين)، وبعضها ممزوج بين الطريقتين (كأصول التحرير لابن الهمام ، والتوضيح لعبيد الله البخارى ، وبديع النظام لنظام الدين الساعاتى)، وهذا كتابنا المسلّم أيضاً من القسم الثالث .
The honor of the science of usul al-fiqh and its excellence through causal proofs (burhan limmi), and here the proof of its honor and excellence through evidential proofs (burhan inni). Burhan limmi is inference from the cause to reach the effect, like inferring from the existence of God the existence of the universe, or inferring from the rising of the sun the existence of day. Burhan inni is inference from the effect to reach the cause, like inferring from the existence of the universe the existence of God, or inferring from the existence of day the rising of the sun. It is known from the above that deriving fiqh from the Book and Sunnah is not easy and possible in actuality except after deep knowledge of the principles of fiqh, and among its principles is the science of usul al-fiqh. So profound knowledge and skill in usul al-fiqh is a cause for understanding fiqh and rulings, and profound knowledge is achieved by taking them from their original sources: the Book and Sunnah. Thus, profound knowledge in usul al-fiqh became a cause for comprehending the issues of fiqh. This is burhan limmi. As for the composition of treatises and sermons in praise of usul al-fiqh, and likewise the authorship of great books and precise investigations in usul al-fiqh and its rules, they are signs and indications and evidential proofs of its honor. That is, the publication by newspaper owners of treatises and newspapers in its praise, and likewise lecturers delivering lectures on its importance and necessity for the ummah, is clear evidence proving the honor of the science of usul al-fiqh and its excellence, just as the authorship of great books with precise investigations in various styles is evidential proof of its honor and excellence among the Islamic sciences. The tanwin (indefinite) in 'kutub' is for glorification and multitude, meaning great and numerous books were authored. What is meant by these books are the usul al-fiqh books of the early scholars like Usul al-Bazdawi, Usul al-Sarakhsi, al-Mustasfa of al-Ghazali, and Mukhtasar Ibn al-Hajib. Some are according to the Hanafi method and some according to the Shafi'i method (as the author pointed to these two methods), and some are mixed between the two methods (like Usul al-Tahrir by Ibn al-Humam, al-Tawdih by Ubayd Allah al-Bukhari, and Badi' al-Nizam by Nizam al-Din al-Sa'ati), and this book of ours 'al-Muslim' is also from the third category.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a methodological introduction that establishes the excellence of usul al-fiqh through two types of proofs: causal (limmi) and evidential (inni). The author first defines each: burhan limmi moves from cause to effect, while burhan inni moves from effect to cause. He applies burhan limmi to show that profound knowledge of usul al-fiqh is the cause for properly understanding fiqh, since fiqh is derived from the primary sources (Quran and Sunnah) only through the principles of usul. Then he applies burhan inni by pointing to the abundance of books, treatises, and lectures praising usul al-fiqh as evidence of its lofty status. The mention of famous usul works from both Hanafi and Shafi'i traditions, as well as mixed works, demonstrates the widespread recognition of this science.

Key Terms
البرهان اللمي (al-burhan al-limmi): Inference from the cause to the effect, used to prove something by its cause.
البرهان الإني (al-burhan al-inni): Inference from the effect to the cause, used to prove something by its signs or effects.
التبحر (al-tabahhur): Profound knowledge and mastery in a science.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the burhan inni used in the passage to prove the excellence of usul al-fiqh?
A) That usul al-fiqh is the cause for understanding fiqh
B) That many books and lectures on usul al-fiqh exist
C) That the sun rises after dawn
D) That fiqh is derived from Quran and Sunnah

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh is proven excellent by two complementary proofs: causal (limmi) as the cause of fiqh understanding, and evidential (inni) through its vast scholarly literature.

Three Types of Muqaddimah in Usul al-Fiqh
Defines three types of introductions: book, science, and proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three types of muqaddimah, distinguish them by their functions, and apply the correct type to a given usul al-fiqh context.

Core Idea
The muqaddimah has three distinct forms: book, science, and proof — each serving a unique purpose in scholarly exposition.

In this passage, the commentator classifies the concept of 'muqaddimah' (preface) into three categories. Understanding these categories is crucial for recognizing the structure of classical usul texts and the role of introductory material. You will learn to identify which type of preface is being used in a given context, especially the preface of the science (muqaddimat al-'ilm), which is the foundation of usul al-fiqh textbooks.

Guided Path
1
Identify the generic definition of muqaddimah
Find the common element: muqaddimah is speech presented before the main subject due to its connection and benefit.
All three types share this basic definition.
2
Distinguish the three types: book, science, proof
Note the scope: muqaddimat al-kitab covers preliminary topics like logic, muqaddimat al-'ilm defines the science itself, and muqaddimat al-dalil consists of the premises of a proof.
Muqaddimat al-'ilm is the one relevant to usul al-fiqh.
3
Recognize the indicator for muqaddimat al-'ilm
The text says the preface that 'gives insight at the beginning' is muqaddimat al-'ilm, which is what the author of Muslim al-Thubut uses.
This type defines the subject, benefit, and name of the science.
4
Understand the structure of muqaddimat al-dalil
This type comprises the minor and major premises (sughra and kubra) used in qiyas, istiqra, and tamthil.
It is the foundational building block of legal reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقدمة وأنواعها
وهي مجموعة الكلام التي تقدم وتذكر أمام المقصود لارتباطها به
وهي ثلاثة أنواع :
-۱ مقدمة الكتاب : وهي عبارة عما يذكر قبل المقصود لارتباطه به ونفعه فيه وعند السيد شريف الجرجاني مقدمة الكتاب (في كتب المنطق ) عبارة عن مباحث اللفظ والدلالة والإفراد والتركيب.
-۲- ومقدّمة العلم : وهي عبارة عن تعريف العلم وبيان موضوعه وفائدته، وهذا هو المراد بالمقدمة هنا، بقرينة قوله : " الكتاب مرتب على مقدمة فيما يفيد البصيرة في الشروع، والمفيد للبصيرة في الشروع إنما تكون مقدّمة العلم .
-٣ ومقدمة الدليل : وهي عبارة عنما يقع جزء الدليل ، أي الصغرى والكبرى اللتين تكونان جزئين من القياس والاستقراء والتمثيل ، ويقال لهما مقدمتي الدليل .
قال الشيخ المارتونكى رحمه الله : والمقصود من قوله : "لا" التنبيه لميان مقاصد الكتاب (وأجزائه) اجمالاً ، ثم التفصيل بقوله : "أما المقدمة الح ، لأن التفصيل بعد : الإجمال أوقع في الذهن.
The preface (muqaddimah) and its types. It is the collection of speech that is presented and mentioned before the intended subject due to its connection with it. It is of three types: 1) The preface of the book: it is what is mentioned before the intended subject due to its connection and benefit for it. According to Sayyid Sharif al-Jurjani, the preface of the book (in books of logic) consists of discussions of utterance, signification, individual terms, and composition. 2) The preface of the science: it is the definition of the science and the clarification of its subject and benefit. This is what is meant by 'the preface' here, indicated by his statement: 'the book is arranged upon a preface concerning what benefits insight at the beginning,' and what benefits insight at the beginning is only the preface of the science. 3) The preface of the proof: it is what constitutes a part of the proof, i.e., the minor and major premises which are parts of analogy, induction, and representation, and they are called the two premises of the proof.
Shaykh al-Martawinki (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The intent of his statement 'la' (no) is to indicate the objectives of the book (and its parts) in brief, then the detail in his statement 'amma al-muqaddimah...' (as for the preface...), because detail after summary is more impactful on the mind.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of the term 'muqaddimah' (preface/introduction). The commentator explains that a muqaddimah is a body of text presented before the main subject because of its connection to it. He then distinguishes three types: (1) Muqaddimat al-kitab: the preface of a book, which includes preliminary discussions; al-Jurjani specifies this in logic as discussions of words, signification, single terms, and composition. (2) Muqaddimat al-'ilm: the preface of a science, which defines the science, its subject, and its benefit. This is the type relevant to usul al-fiqh, as indicated by the author of 'Muslim al-Thubut' when he says the book begins with a preface that gives insight. (3) Muqaddimat al-dalil: the preface of a proof, which consists of the minor and major premises of an argument (sughra and kubra) used in analogy, induction, and example. These two premises are called 'muqaddimat al-dalil'. The commentator ends with a quote from Shaykh al-Martawinki, who clarifies that the author's use of 'la' (no) in the text signals a brief enumeration of the book's objectives, followed by detailed explanation for better retention.

Key Terms
مقدمة الكتاب (muqaddimat al-kitab): What is mentioned before the intended subject of the book due to connection and benefit.
مقدمة العلم (muqaddimat al-'ilm): Definition of the science, its subject, and its benefit.
مقدمة الدليل (muqaddimat al-dalil): The minor and major premises of a proof (sughra and kubra).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which type of muqaddimah is intended when referring to the preface of 'Muslim al-Thubut'?
A) Muqaddimat al-kitab
B) Muqaddimat al-'ilm
C) Muqaddimat al-dalil
D) All three equally

Key Takeaway
Identifying the correct type of muqaddimah is essential for understanding the structure and purpose of a scholarly text in usul al-fiqh.

Distinction Between Book Introduction and Science Introduction
Exposition of the dual meaning of 'muqaddimah' and the three pillars of the science introduction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between muqaddimat al-kitab and muqaddimat al-ilm, and identify the three essential components of the latter (definition, subject, and benefit).

Core Idea
The science introduction is defined by three pillars; the book preface is merely a textual device.

In scholarly works, the term 'introduction' can refer either to the conceptual prerequisites for studying a science or to the preliminary remarks of a book. This passage clarifies that the phrase 'an introduction that benefits insight' points to the science introduction, which consists of three key elements: definition, subject, and benefit. Understanding this distinction helps the learner approach a science with proper perspective.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Phrase and Its Context
The author begins by quoting the phrase 'مقدمة في ما يفيد البصيرة' from the base text. We must determine what 'introduction' (مقدمة) means here.
The phrase itself does not specify which type of introduction is meant.
2
Apply the Contextual Clue
The phrase 'فيها يفيد البصيرة' (in which it benefits insight) indicates that this introduction provides insight, which is characteristic of the science introduction, not the book preface.
The word 'يفيد' (benefits) is key—it suggests a conceptual gain beyond mere textual placement.
3
Contrast with Book Introduction
The author defines the book introduction as a set of statements placed before the main content due to their connection and benefit, whereas the science introduction is the preliminary knowledge needed to begin the science with insight.
Book introductions are specific to a text; science introductions are universal to the discipline.
4
List the Three Components of Science Introduction
The science introduction consists of three elements: knowledge of the definition (حد), the subject (موضوع), and the benefit (غاية) of the science.
These are the pillars that provide complete insight.
5
Understand the Benefit of These Components
Knowledge of the definition removes absolute ignorance; knowing the subject distinguishes this science from others; knowing the purpose ensures effort is not in vain.
The example of morphology and grammar illustrates how purpose motivates learning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : مقدمة في ما يفيد البصيرة والمراد بالمقدمة مقدمة العلم بقرينة قوله (فيها يفيد البصيرة) وهي عبارة عن تعريف العلم وفائدته وبيان موضوعه . وأما مقدمة الكتاب فهى عبارة عن طائفة من الكلام تذكر أمام المقصود لارتباطها به ونفعها فيه . ومصداقها إما الألفاظ المخصوصة الدالة على المعانى ، وإمّا المعانى المخصوصة المدلولة ، وإما كلاهما (الألفاظ والمعانى (المخصوصة أما احتمال النقوش منفردةً ومجتمعةً فغير معتبر في الكتاب، وبما أنّ المقدمة جزء من الكتاب ، يعلم من قوله : فيها يفيد البصيرة، أن المراد بها مقدمة العلم ، وهي ما يتوقف عليه الشروع في العلم على وجه البصيرة الكاملة . ومصداق مقدمة العلم هي الأمور ـة العلم هي الأمور الثلاثة : -۱- معرفة حد العلم (تعريفه) ٢- ومعرفة موضوعه ، أي التصديق بكون شيئ موضوعاً للعلم ، لا الموضوع نفسه فقط، وهو مفرد لا يتعلق به التصديق. ٣- ومعرفة الغاية ، أي التصديق بكونها غاية للعلم ، إذ الغاية المفردة لا تصلح أن تكون متعلّقا للتصديق إذ التصديق لا يتعلق بالمفرد. ولكن لو كان المراد بالمقدمة) الألفاظ المخصوصة الدالة على المعانى المخصوصة وقُطِعَ النظر عن قوله ( فيما يفيد البصيرة) يراد بها مقدمة الكتاب . أما لو كان المراد بها المعانى المخصوصة ، أو المعاني والألفاظ كلتيهما يكون المراد بالمقدمة مقدمة العلم التي هي عبارة عن تعريف العلم والتصديق بموضوعه وفائدته ، بدليل قوله ( فيما يفيد البصيرة). وهذه الثلاث إنما تحصل من المعانى المدلولة الخاصة وتكون المقدمة مفيدة للبصيرة الكاملة إذا حصلت منها العلوم الثلاثة : علم بتعريفه وموضوعه وغايته . فائدة : حد العلم وموضوعه وغايته فمعرفة حد العلم يخرج المتعلم عن طلب المجهول المطلق ، وبمعرفة موضوعه يمتاز العلم المشروع فيه ( عند الطالب ) عن غيره ، وبمعرفة غايته لا يكون سعيه عبثاً . المثال التطبيقي : فإن غاية علم الصرف معرفة مادة الكلمة (من الحروف الأصلية والزائدة ، ومن الصحيحة والعلة) ومعرفة هئيتها من الحركات المختلفة والشكون، والغاية لعلم النحو هي صيانة اللسان والقلم عن الخطأ اللفظي والمعنوي. ۱ - فإذا علم المتعلّم غاية العلم يظهر الشوق والرغبة في تعلمه، ويسعى في تحصيل ذلك العلم المشروع فيه . وكذا إذا علم موضوع العلم المشروع فيه يميز بين العلم المطلوب وغير المطلوب، فان تمايز العلوم بتمايز الموضوعات و موضوع كلّ علم ما يبحث فيه عن عوارضه الذاتية ، واثبات تلك العوارض لموضوع العلم هي مسألة من مسائل ذلك العلم ، فيكون العلم بالموضوع سبباً للعلم بمسائل العلم المشروع فيه إجمالاً، وإذا ذكرت مسائل العلم تفصيلاً تكون أوقع في الذهن ، إذا الإجمال بعد التفصيل يفيد البصيرة الزائدة والعلم الوافر .
His statement: 'An introduction that benefits insight.' The intended meaning of 'introduction' is the introduction to the science, indicated by his statement 'in which it benefits insight.' It consists of the definition of the science, its benefit, and the explanation of its subject matter. As for the introduction to the book, it is a set of statements placed before the main objective due to their connection to it and benefit in it. Its referent is either the specific words indicating the meanings, or the specific meanings indicated, or both (the specific words and meanings). As for the possibility of individual or combined marks (letters), it is not considered in the book. Since the introduction is part of the book, it is known from his statement 'in which it benefits insight' that what is meant is the introduction to the science, upon which commencing the science with complete insight depends. The referent of the introduction to the science consists of three things: 1. Knowledge of the definition of the science (its definition). 2. Knowledge of its subject matter, i.e., affirming that something is the subject of the science, not merely the subject itself—which is a singular noun that does not engage affirmation. 3. Knowledge of its purpose, i.e., affirming that it is the purpose of the science, for a singular purpose cannot be the object of affirmation because affirmation does not attach to singular concepts. But if what is meant by 'introduction' is the specific words indicating specific meanings, and one disregards his statement 'in which it benefits insight,' then it refers to the introduction to the book. However, if what is meant is the specific meanings, or both meanings and words, then the reference is the introduction to the science, which consists of the definition of the science and affirming its subject and benefit, evidenced by his statement 'in which it benefits insight.' These three are only obtained from the specific indicated meanings, and the introduction benefits complete insight if from it are obtained the three sciences: knowledge of its definition, its subject, and its purpose. Benefit: The definition of a science, its subject, and its purpose. Knowledge of the definition of a science removes the learner from seeking the absolutely unknown; by knowing its subject, the science being undertaken (for the student) is distinguished from others; by knowing its purpose, his effort is not in vain. Applied example: The purpose of the science of morphology is to know the root of a word (original and extra letters, sound and weak letters) and to know its form with regard to different vowel signs and sukoons. The purpose of the science of grammar is to safeguard the tongue and pen from verbal and grammatical error. 1. When a learner knows the purpose of a science, desire and eagerness to learn it appear, and he strives to acquire that science being undertaken. Similarly, when he knows the subject of the science being undertaken, he differentiates between the desired science and what is not desired, for sciences are differentiated by the differentiation of their subject matters. The subject of every science is that in which it investigates its essential accidents; proving those accidents for the subject of the science is a particular issue of that science. Knowledge of the subject becomes a cause for knowing the issues of the science being undertaken in summary, and when the issues of the science are mentioned in detail, they are more impactful in the mind because summary after detail yields additional insight and abundant knowledge.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the term 'muqaddimah' (introduction) as used in the context of a scholarly work. The author clarifies that the phrase 'introduction that benefits insight' refers to the introduction to the science itself, not merely the introductory section of the book. He explains that the introduction to a science has three components: defining the science, identifying its subject matter, and stating its benefit or purpose. These three elements equip the learner with the necessary perspective to embark on the science with full insight. The author contrasts this with the introduction to a book, which is merely a set of preliminary statements. He further illustrates with examples from Arabic morphology (sarf) and grammar (nahw) to show how knowing the purpose of a science motivates the student and how knowing the subject matter distinguishes one science from another. The passage emphasizes that summary knowledge after detailed explanation enhances understanding.

Key Terms
مقدمة العلم (muqaddimat al-ʿilm): The introductory knowledge required before studying a science, consisting of its definition, subject, and benefit.
مقدمة الكتاب (muqaddimat al-kitāb): A set of preliminary statements placed before the main content of a book, connected to it and beneficial for it.
حد العلم (ḥadd al-ʿilm): The definition of a science that distinguishes it from other sciences and from absolute ignorance.
موضوع العلم (mawḍūʿ al-ʿilm): The specific subject matter that a science investigates in terms of its essential accidents.
غاية العلم (ghāyat al-ʿilm): The ultimate purpose or benefit of studying a science.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what are the three components of the introduction to a science (مقدمة العلم)?
A) Words, meanings, and marks
B) Definition, subject, and purpose
C) Book, science, and benefit
D) Summary, detail, and insight

Key Takeaway
The introduction to a science (مقدمة العلم) is defined by its three essential components — definition, subject, and benefit — which together provide the insight necessary to begin studying that science.

The Two Definitions of Usul al-Fiqh
Defining the two definitions of usul al-fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the attributive definition (iḍāfī) and the title definition (laqabī) of Uṣūl al-Fiqh and explain the benefit of each.

Core Idea
Uṣūl al-Fiqh has two definitions: one by breaking down the words, and one as a proper name for a science.

In this passage, the commentator explains that the term 'Uṣūl al-Fiqh' can be defined in two ways: either as an attributive compound (defining each word separately) or as a title for a specific science. Understanding this distinction is foundational for grasping the scope of the discipline.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions mentioned
Locate where the commentator says 'the author mentioned for usul al-fiqh two definitions'. Note that one is attributive (iḍāfī) and the other is a title (laqabī).
2
Explain the attributive definition
The attributive definition defines the compound by defining its parts: 'uṣūl' (principles) and 'al-fiqh' (jurisprudence). Understand that this gives a literal meaning: the principles of jurisprudence.
3
Explain the title definition
The title definition treats 'Uṣūl al-Fiqh' as a proper name for a specific science, like 'biology' or 'grammar'. It no longer requires a word-by-word breakdown.
4
Determine which is intended
The commentator states that what is intended here is the second definition (title definition). This is because the science has its own distinct subject matter and methodology.
5
Apply the benefit
The benefit of the two definitions is clarification: understanding both helps avoid confusion between the literal meaning and the technical field.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يمتاز العلم المشروع فيه ( عند الطالب ) عن غيره ، وبمعرفة غايته لا يكون سعيه عبثاً . المثال التطبيقي : فإن غاية علم الصرف معرفة مادة الكلمة (من الحروف الأصلية والزائدة ، ومن الصحيحة والعلة) ومعرفة هئيتها من الحركات المختلفة والشكون، والغاية لعلم النحو هي صيانة اللسان والقلم عن الخطأ اللفظي والمعنوي. ۱ - فإذا علم المتعلّم غاية العلم يظهر الشوق والرغبة في تعلمه، ويسعى في تحصيل ذلك العلم المشروع فيه . وكذا إذا علم موضوع العلم المشروع فيه يميز بين العلم المطلوب وغير المطلوب، فان تمايز العلوم بتمايز الموضوعات و موضوع كلّ علم ما يبحث فيه عن عوارضه الذاتية ، واثبات تلك العوارض لموضوع العلم هي مسألة من مسائل ذلك العلم ، فيكون العلم بالموضوع سبباً للعلم بمسائل العلم المشروع فيه إجمالاً، وإذا ذكرت مسائل العلم تفصيلاً تكون أوقع في الذهن ، إذا الإجمال بعد التفصيل يفيد البصيرة الزائدة والعلم الوافر . ثم بعد الفراغ عن ذكر أجزاء الكتاب اجمالأشرع في تفصيلها وقال: أما المقدمة ففي حد أصول الفقه، وموضوعه وفائدته أما حده مضافاً فالأصل لغة ما يبتنى عليه غيره واصطلاحاً له أربعة معان الراجح والمستصحب والقاعد والدليل واعلم أنّ المصنف ذكر لأصول الفقه تعريفين : إضافياً : وهو تعريف المضاف (الأصول أولاً ، وتعريف المضاف إليه (الفقه) ثانياً . ولقبياً : وهو كون المركب (أصول الفقه) لقب لعلم مخصوص وفائدة التعريفين التوضيح ، والتنبيه على أن المطلوب هنا التعريف الثاني وهو اللقبي. تعريف الأصل لغة واصطلاحا فقال في تعريف الأصل (الذى جمعه أصول): الأصل في اللغة ما يبتنى عليه غيره، كالأساس الذى يبتنى عليه الجدار ، حسّاً ، وكالقاعدة التي يبتنى عليها الجزئيات عقلاً ، كما أن الفرع هو لغة ما يبتنى على غيره وهو الأصل. الحقيقة. وهو في الاصطلاح يأتي على أربعة معان: الراجح، والمستصحب والقاعدة والدليل. مثال الراجح ، كقولهم : الحقيقة أصل بالنسبة إلى المجاز ، أو الأصل في الكلام ومثال المستصحب (استصحاب الحال جعل الحالة السابقة باقية ودليلاً على الحكم في زمان الحال ، وإجراء الحكم عليه كالسابق ، كما يقال الأصل في الماء الطهارة ، والنجاسة طارئة . ومثال القاعدة : كقولهم : الفاعل مرفوع ، والمفعول منصوب ، وهما أصلان من أصول النحو ومثال الدليل قول الفقهاء : الأصل في الطهارة ، قوله تعالى: (إذا قمتم إلى الصلاة فاغسلوا وجوهكم ) الآية. شرح مفردات عبارة المصنف ١ - كلمة أما تستعمل لتفصيل الاحمال السابق ، نحو قولك جاءني زيد وعمرو و بكر ، أما زيد فأكرمته ، وأما عمرو فأخرجته من المنزل، وأما بكر فألبسته ثوباً، ونحو ذلك . ولما ذكر المصنف أجزاء الكتاب إجمالاً ففضلها وبين فائدة كل جزء منها مستقلاً فقال : ٢ - أما المقدمة: معرّفاً باللام بعد ذكرها نكرة في الإجمال ، فهي عين المقدمة المذكورة في السابق . وقوله : " ففي حد أصول الفقه على تقدير المضاف ، أي ففي معرفة حد أصول الفقه وموضوعه وفائدته ، والباعث على تقدير المضاف أن نفس وجود الحد
The prescribed knowledge is distinguished (for the student) from other knowledge, and by knowing its goal his effort is not in vain. Applied example: the goal of morphology is knowledge of the word's material (original and additional letters, sound and weak) and knowledge of its form from different movements and pauses, and the goal of syntax is guarding the tongue and pen from verbal and grammatical error. 1. When the student knows the goal of a knowledge, desire and inclination to learn it appear, and he strives to acquire that prescribed knowledge. Likewise, if he knows the subject matter of the prescribed knowledge, he distinguishes between desired and undesired knowledge, for sciences are differentiated by their subject matters. The subject matter of every science is that in which its essential accidents are investigated, and establishing those accidents for the subject matter is a problem of that science. Knowledge of the subject matter is a cause for knowledge of the problems of the prescribed knowledge in summary, and when the problems of a science are mentioned in detail, they are more impactful in the mind, because summary after detail provides increased insight and abundant knowledge. The benefit of the two definitions is clarification and drawing attention to the fact that what is intended here is the second definition, the title definition. Commentary
This passage is an introductory explanation from a commentary on a Hanafi usul al-fiqh text. The author first discusses the importance of knowing the goal (ghāyah) and subject (mawḍūʿ) of a science, illustrating with examples from Arabic morphology (ṣarf) and syntax (naḥw). He then transitions to the book's structure, noting that the author of the matn lists the parts of the book in summary before detailing them. The focus shifts to the definition of 'uṣūl al-fiqh'. The commentator explains that there are two definitions: an attributive definition (taʿrīf iḍāfī) which defines the two words separately—'al-uṣūl' (principles) and 'al-fiqh' (jurisprudence)—and a title definition (taʿrīf laqabī) where the compound 'uṣūl al-fiqh' is a proper name for a specific science. The intended definition is the latter. The commentator then defines the word 'aṣl' (plural: uṣūl) linguistically as 'that on which something else is built', comparable to a foundation for a wall (physical) or a rule for particulars (intellectual). Terminologically, 'aṣl' has four distinct meanings in Hanafi usul: (1) al-rājiḥ (the preponderant interpretation over weaker ones, e.g., literal over figurative), (2) al-mustaṣḥab (the presumption of continuity, e.g., the original ruling of purity in water), (3) al-qāʿidah (a general principle or rule, e.g., grammatical rules like subject raising), and (4) al-dalīl (an evidence or proof, e.g., a Qur'anic verse as proof for purification rules). The commentator then analytically breaks down the phrase 'ammā al-muqaddimah', explaining that 'ammā' is used for detailing a previous summary, and that the introduction is the same as previously mentioned. The explanation ends mid-sentence with an analysis of the author's words about the definition of uṣūl al-fiqh on the premise of an implied genitive construction.

Key Terms
أصول الفقه (uṣūl al-fiqh): A title definition: the science that deals with the sources of Islamic law and methods of derivation. An attributive definition: 'uṣūl' (principles) + 'al-fiqh' (jurisprudence).

The Four Technical Meanings of 'Asl' in Hanafi Usul
Defining the four technical meanings of 'asl'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify each of the four technical meanings of 'aṣl' (al-rājiḥ, al-mustaṣḥab, al-qāʿidah, al-dalīl) and provide an example for each from the text.

Core Idea
'Aṣl' has four distinct meanings in usul: preponderant, continual, principle, and evidence.

The word 'aṣl' is used frequently in usul texts, but its meaning shifts. This passage clarifies that in Hanafi terminology, 'aṣl' can refer to the preponderant interpretation, the presumption of continuity, a general rule, or a source of evidence. Recognizing these meanings prevents confusion when reading usul works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four meanings listed
Locate the phrase 'terminologically it has four meanings: al-rājiḥ, al-mustaṣḥab, al-qāʿidah, al-dalīl'. Write them down.
2
Understand 'al-rājiḥ' (the preponderant)
This meaning refers to the stronger or more likely interpretation. Example: the literal meaning (ḥaqīqah) is the aṣl compared to the figurative (majāz).
3
Understand 'al-mustaṣḥab' (the presumed continuity)
This is a presumption that a previous state continues until evidence shows otherwise. Example: water is originally pure; impurity is accidental.
4
Understand 'al-qāʿidah' (the principle/rule)
A general rule that applies to many cases, like grammatical rules: 'the subject is raised'.
5
Understand 'al-dalīl' (the evidence)
A source or proof. Example: the Qur'anic verse about wudu is the aṣl for purification rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Definition of a Science: Hadd, Tasawwur, and Tasdiq
Expanding on the meaning of hadd and the role of tasawwur/tasdiq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two types of hadd and explain why knowledge of a science's subject and goal requires tasdiq not just tasawwur.

Core Idea
Knowing a science's subject and goal is not enough; you must affirm them as such.

This passage from a commentary on usul al-fiqh clarifies what is meant by a 'definition' (hadd) of a science. It distinguishes between conceptual knowledge (tasawwur) of the definition itself and affirmatory knowledge (tasdiq) of the subject matter and goal. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly framing the study of any discipline, especially usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two meanings of hadd
Identify that 'hadd' can mean either an absolute inclusive/exclusive definition (jāmiʿ māniʿ) or a real definition composed of genus and differentia. The passage explains that definitions of sciences are of the real type because sciences are conceptual quiddities (mahiyat i'tibariyyah).
The internal elements of a science's definition are essential (dhati), external ones are accidental (ʿaradi).
2
Clarify what ‘knowledge of the definition’ means
Recognize that ‘knowledge of the definition’ is conceptual (tasawwur): you need a mental concept of the definition itself, e.g., the definition of usul al-fiqh.
This is not yet a judgment; it is simply grasping the term.
3
Understand why subject and goal require tasdiq
The subject (mawḍūʿ) and goal (ghāyah) are singular terms (mufradāt). As singulars, they cannot be the object of tasdiq directly. Instead, we need tasdiq to affirm that a particular thing IS the subject or goal of this science.
Tasdiq here means affirming a relationship, not the term itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إزالة الرهبوت عن مشكلات مسلم الثبوت والموضوع والغاية لا تفيد البصيرة من غير معرفتها تفصيلاً، والمراد من الحد وغيره هو معرفة الحد وتصديق بالموضوع والغاية ، لا نفس وجودها من غير معرفة وتصديق . ولا شك أن معرفة هذه الأمور تفيد البصيرة .
٤- والمراد بالحد إما مطلق التعريف الجامع المانع ، وإما المراد به الحد الحقيقي المركب من الجنس والفصل؛ لأن تعريف العلوم ماهيات اعتبارية، فما اعتبر داخلاً فيها يكون ذاتيالها ، وما اعتبر خارجاً عنها يكون عرضياً لها .
قال الشيخ المارتونكى رحمه الله : ثم المراد بمعرفة الحد معرفته التصوري أي العلم بتعريفه (تعريف أصول الفقه ، وبمعرفة الموضوع التصديق بموضوعية الموضوع ،بأن هذا الشئ موضوع لهذا العلم ، لأنّ نفس الموضوع مفرد ، لا يتعلّق به التصديق ، وكذا المراد بمعرفة الغاية التصديق بها ، أي التصديق بأن هذا الشي غاية لهذا العلم. إذ الغاية أيضاً مفردة ، لا يتعلّق بها التصديق . انتهى
وقد مر أن تعريف العلوم بالماهيات الاعتبارية تعريف بالحد لها ، إذ المفهومات المعتبرة في تعريفاتها كالذاتيات لها ، وليس المعتبر في تعريفاتها الأجزاء الخارجية ، حتى يرد الإشكال على كون تعريفاتها حداً ؛ بأن الحد بالأجزاء الخارجية تعريف بالرسم وبالعرض ، و بأن الحد بأجزاء الشيئ خارجية كانت أو داخلية، كتعريف الشئ بنفسه ، فالتعريف الاضافي منقول عنه ، والتعريف اللقبي منقول إليه، وسيأتي بيان المناسبة بين المنقول عنه والمنقول إليه في قول المصنف : "ثم هذا العلم أدلة اجمالية".
The removal of fear from the difficulties of Musallam al-Thubut: The subject and the goal do not give insight without detailed knowledge of them. What is meant by the definition (hadd) and other things is knowledge of the definition and affirmation of the subject and the goal, not their mere existence without knowledge and affirmation. There is no doubt that knowledge of these things gives insight.
4- By 'definition' is meant either an absolute comprehensive and exclusive definition, or the real definition composed of genus and differentia; because definitions of sciences are from conceptual quiddities (mahiyat i'tibariyyah), so what is considered internal to them is essential (dhati) to them, and what is considered external to them is accidental ('aradi) to them.
Shaykh al-Martunqi (may Allah have mercy on him) said: Then by 'knowledge of the definition' is meant its conceptual knowledge, i.e., knowledge of its definition (the definition of usul al-fiqh), and by 'knowledge of the subject' is meant the affirmation of the subject-hood of the subject, that this thing is the subject of this science, because the subject itself is a singular term, and affirmation does not pertain to it. Similarly, by 'knowledge of the goal' is meant affirmation of it, i.e., the affirmation that this thing is the goal of this science. For the goal is also a singular term, and affirmation does not pertain to it. End.
And it has passed that the definition of sciences by conceptual quiddities is a definition by definition (hadd) for them, because the concepts considered in their definitions are like essential properties for them, and what is considered in their definitions is not the external parts, such that an objection might arise that their definitions are definitions (hadd) because a definition by external parts is a definition by description (rasm) and by accident, and because a definition by parts of a thing, whether external or internal, is like defining a thing by itself. So the relational definition (ta'rif idafi) is transferred from it, and the titular definition (ta'rif laqabi) is transferred to it, and an explanation of the relationship between the transferred-from and the transferred-to will come in the author's statement: 'Then this science is the total evidence (adillah ijmaliyyah).'
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the beginning of a work on usul al-fiqh. It explains that simply knowing the subject and goal of a science is insufficient without detailed knowledge (tasawwur) and affirmation (tasdiq). The author distinguishes between two types of definition (hadd): an absolute inclusive/exclusive definition, and a real definition consisting of genus and differentia. Since sciences are conceptual (i'tibari), their definitions are considered hadd, with internal elements being essential (dhati) and external elements accidental ('aradi). The quote from Shaykh al-Martunqi clarifies that knowledge of the definition is conceptual (tasawwur), while knowledge of the subject and goal is affirmatory (tasdiq) because subject and goal are singular terms that cannot be known by tasdiq alone. The passage then addresses a potential objection: that defining sciences by conceptual quiddities is not a real hadd because it uses external parts. The response is that definitions of sciences are based on internal concepts, not external parts, so they are genuine hadd. The relational and titular definitions are also mentioned, with a promise to explain their connection to the author's upcoming statement about usul al-fiqh being 'total evidence.'

Key Terms
الحد (al-hadd): Either an absolute definition (jāmiʿ māniʿ) or a real definition composed of genus and differentia.
التصوري (al-tasawwuri): Conceptual knowledge, i.e., knowledge of a definition without judgment.
التصديق (al-tasdiq): Affirmatory knowledge, i.e., judgment that something is the subject or goal of a science.
الموضوع (al-mawḍūʿ): The subject matter of a science, considered as a singular term.
الغاية (al-ghāyah): The goal or purpose of a science, also a singular term.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the subject and goal are complex concepts requiring detailed analysis.
B) Because the subject and goal are singular terms, and tasdiq is not applicable to singular terms directly.
C) Because the subject and goal are singular terms, and tasdiq is needed to affirm that they are the subject or goal of the science.
D) Because the author prefers tasdiq over tasawwur in all definitions.

Key Takeaway
Defining a science requires both conceptual knowledge (tasawwur) of its definition and affirmatory knowledge (tasdiq) of its subject and goal.

The Meaning of 'Usul' in Usul al-Fiqh: Proofs vs Rules
Defining usul al-fiqh and correcting a common misunderstanding

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the meaning of 'usul' in 'usul al-fiqh' and apply the principle of idafah to distinguish proofs from rules.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, 'usul al-fiqh' means the proofs of fiqh, not its rules.

This passage tackles a foundational question: what exactly does 'usul' mean in 'usul al-fiqh'? The author insists that when 'asl' is added to a science, it refers to the proofs (adillah) of that science, not its rules. He then refutes a contrary view and explains how the term 'rules' can still appear in the definition in a different sense. By the end, you will grasp the precise Hanafi understanding and see how it shapes the entire science of usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic principle
The author states a general rule: when 'asl' (singular of 'usul') is added to a science via construct phrase (idafah), it means the proof (dalil) of that science. For example, 'usul al-tafsir' means the proofs of tafsir, not the rules of tafsir.
This principle is key to understanding the Hanafi position.
2
State the two positions
Some usulis, like the author of al-Tawdih, interpret 'usul' in 'usul al-fiqh' as 'rules' (qawa'id). The Hanafi position, defended by our author, is that it means 'proofs'.
The dispute is about the correct interpretation of the idafah.
3
Understand the refutation
The author gives two reasons why the 'rules' interpretation is wrong: (1) it ignores the established linguistic principle that 'asl' in idafah means proof; (2) if 'usul' meant rules, it would be redundant because the rules of a science are its very issues (masa'il), not its preliminaries.
This refutation relies on the distinction between the subject matter of a science and its foundational principles.
4
Recognize the lexical flexibility
The author concedes that lexically, 'asl' can mean both proof and rule. However, in the terminological idafah, it is fixed as proof. This prevents confusion when reading different definitions.
The lexical meaning is broader, but the technical usage limits it.
5
Apply the definition with example
The author defines usul al-fiqh as 'a science of rules by which the mujtahid derives fiqh rulings.' Here 'rules' refers to the usuli principles (like 'command indicates obligation'), not the rules of fiqh. He then illustrates with the derivation of zakat obligation: the detailed proof (verse) plus the general proof (the usuli rule) yields the ruling.
The example shows how general proofs (adillah ijmaaliyah) operate in practice.
