Four Possibilities for Defining Quiddity and Their Invalidity
Analyzing four invalid ways to define quiddity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four possibilities for defining quiddity and explain why each leads to the logical fallacy of tahsil al-hasil or priority.

Core Idea
Defining quiddity by itself or its parts is futile; only formal definition by special property can distinguish.

The author analyzes all possible ways to define the essence of a thing. He shows that each leads to either circularity (tahsil al-hasil) or logical priority. However, formal definition using special properties can serve to distinguish the thing even if it does not convey the essence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four possibilities
List the four ways a quiddity might be defined: by itself, by all its parts, by some parts, or by accidents.
2
Understand tahsil al-hasil
Define the fallacy of 'attaining the obtained' and see how it applies to defining by itself. Also note the priority issue.
3
Apply refutation to each
For each possibility, see why it is invalid: 1) tahsil al-hasil, 2) same as 1, plus priority, 3) even worse, 4) accidents cannot give essence.
4
Recognize exception for formal definition
Note that formal definition using special properties can provide distinction, though not essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو تحصيل الحاصل وأما التعريف الرسمي الذي يكون بالعوارض، فلا تتحصل به الحقيقة، نعم يمكن به بالتعريف الرسمى امتياز الحقيقة عنما عداها إذا كان بالخواص دون العرض العام .
ووجه لزوم تحصيل الحاصل بالتعريف أن تعريف ماهية من الماهيات أو حقيقة من الحقائق ( فإن الماهية هي الحقيقة بعد وقوعها في جواب السؤال بـ ( ما هي ؟ ) لا يخلو عن أحد من الاحتمالات الأربعة :
إما أن يكون تعريفها بنفسها، وإما أن يكون بجميع أجزائها، وإما أن يكون ببعض أجزائها، أو يكون بعوارضها، والكل باطل .
-١ أما بطلان الشق الأول، فإنّ تعريف الشيئ بنفسه تحصيل الحاصل، أي تحصيل الشيئ الذى كان حاصلاً من قبل، وهذا الغو، وأيضاً يلزم تقدم الشيئ (من حيث أنه معزف بالكسر ) على نفسه من حيث أنه معرّف بالفتح ) فإن الحد يكون مقدماً على المحدود.
۲ وأما الشق الثاني، فلأن جميع الأجزاء هو نفس الشيئ تفصيلاً، فيكون التعريف بها هو التعريف بنفس الشيئ مع لزوم المحال فيه أيضاً (وهو تقدم الشيئ على نفسه وتقدم الأجزاء على الكل.
-٣- وأما الشق الثالث، فلأن الكل (جميع الأجزاء) إذا لم يفد المعرفة، بل يلزم فيه تقدم الشيئ على نفسه، وتقدم الأجزاء كلاً أو بعضاً على الكل ممنوع، فكيف التعريف ببعض الأجزاء؟
-٤- وأما الشق الرابع ، ( وهو التعريف بالعوارض)، فإنه لا يمكن معرفة الحقيقة بالعوارض الخارجة عنها، فإنها لا تفيد علم الحقيقة، نعم يحصل بها امتياز الحقيقة عن جميع ما عداها إذا كانت العوارض من الخواص، وإلا فلا، فثبت أن تعريف الماهية (الحقيقة) غير ممكن بالتعريف الحقيقي ولا بالرسمى
تفصيل الجواب : أن التصورات المتعلقة بالأجزاء، أي أجزاء الحد تفصيلاً مثل تصور الحيوان، وتصور الناطق في تعريف الإنسان أو تصور اللفظ والوضع والمعنى والإفراد في تعريف الكلمة، إذا رتبت بتقدم العام على الخاص، وقيدت بجعل الخاص صفة للعام، حتى يحصل المركب التقييدى، فهذا المجموع المرتب المقيد (سواء كان له جزآن أو أكثر ) هو الحد الموصل إلى الصورة الواحدانية التى حصلت للحد ( بعد الهيئة التركيبية) وتعلقت بجميع أجزاء الحد اجمالاً، وهو أي مجموع الصور المتعلقة بأجزاء الحد، والتى عرضت لها الصورة الوحدانية بعد الترتيب والتركيب المحدود، وهذا المجموع المرتب المركب لم يكن حاصلاً من قبل فههنا أي في محلّ التعريف الحقيقى) تحصيل أمر (وهو العلم بالمجموع ) لم يكن حاصلاً قبل هذا الترتيب والتقييد والتركيب .
فتدبر : فيه إشارة إلى جواب آخر، وهو أن منع التعريف للماهية باعتبار العوارض ممنوع ؛ لأن الغرض من تعريف الماهية قد يكون تحصيل حقيقتها، ولاشك أن هذا الغرض لا يحصل من التعريف بالعوارض ؛ إذ لا تحصل الحقيقة بها ؛ وقد يكون الغرض من تعريفها امتيازها عن جميع ما عداها وهذا الغرض يحصل من التعريف بالرسم (بالعوارض) فالحكم بمنع التعريف الحقيقي حداً ورسماً ممنوع بهذا السند المذكور.
And it is attainment of the obtained. As for the formal definition (rasmi) which is by accidents, the essence is not attained by it. Yes, by formal definition it is possible to distinguish the essence from what is other than it if it is by special properties (khawass) and not by common accident. The reason for the necessity of attainment of the obtained by definition is that defining a quiddity among quiddities or a reality among realities (for quiddity is reality after it occurs in answer to the question 'what is it?') is not free from one of four possibilities: either it is defined by itself, or by all its parts, or by some of its parts, or by its accidents. All are invalid. As for the invalidity of the first branch: defining a thing by itself is attainment of the obtained, i.e., attaining something that was already obtained, and this is futile. Also, it requires the priority of the thing (as definiendum) over itself (as definition) for the definition precedes the defined. As for the second branch: because all parts are the thing itself in detail, so defining by them is defining by the thing itself, along with the impossibility also involved (priority of the thing over itself and priority of parts over the whole). As for the third branch: because the whole (all parts) if it does not give knowledge, rather there is in it priority of the thing over itself and priority of parts, whole or some, over the whole is prevented, so how can defining by some parts be? As for the fourth branch (definition by accidents): it is impossible to know the reality by accidents external to it, for they do not give knowledge of the reality. Yes, by them distinction of the reality from all others is obtained if the accidents are special properties; otherwise no. So it is established that defining quiddity (reality) is not possible by real definition nor by formal definition. Detailed answer: the conceptualizations related to the parts, i.e., the parts of the limit in detail, such as the conceptualization of animal and the conceptualization of rational in the definition of human, or the conceptualization of word, meaning, and singularity in the definition of kalima, when arranged with the general preceding the specific, and restricted by making the specific a description of the general, until the restrictive compound is obtained, then this arranged restricted composite (whether it has two parts or more) is the limit that leads to the unitary form that occurs to the limit (after the composite structure) and is related to all parts of the limit in summary. And it, i.e., the set of forms related to the parts of the limit, which are subject to the unitary form after arrangement and composition of the defined, was not obtained before. So here (in the place of real definition) there is attainment of something (knowledge of the composite) that was not obtained before this arrangement, restriction, and composition. So reflect: in it there is an indication of another answer, which is that the prevention of definition of quiddity by accidents is prevented; because the purpose of defining quiddity may be to attain its reality, and there is no doubt that this purpose is not obtained from definition by accidents, since reality is not attained by them; and the purpose of defining it may be to distinguish it from all others, and this purpose is obtained from definition by drawing (by accidents). So the judgment that real definition is prevented, both by essential and formal definition, is prevented by this mentioned chain.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of the definition of quiddity (mahiyyah) in the context of Islamic epistemology and usul al-fiqh. The author first distinguishes between real definition (ta'rif haqiqi) which aims to convey the essence, and formal definition (ta'rif rasmi) which uses accidents to distinguish the thing. He then presents four possible ways to define a quiddity: by itself, by all its parts, by some parts, or by accidents. Each is shown to be problematic. The first three involve circularity or infinite regress (tahsil al-hasil). The fourth, using accidents, cannot convey the essence itself but can provide distinction if the accidents are special properties (khawass). The author then provides a refined answer: the conceptualizations of the parts, when arranged properly, produce a composite that was not previously known, thus avoiding circularity. Finally, he notes that even definition by accidents is not entirely useless; it serves the purpose of distinction. This discussion is foundational for understanding how scholars define legal terms in usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
تعريف حقيقي (ta'rif haqiqi): Definition that conveys the essence of a thing through its essential parts.
تعريف رسمي (ta'rif rasmi): Definition that distinguishes a thing through its accidents or properties, without conveying the essence.
تحصيل الحاصل (tahsil al-hasil): Logical fallacy of achieving what is already achieved, i.e., circular definition.
ماهية (mahiyyah): Quiddity; the essence of a thing, what it is in answer to 'what is it?'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the four possibilities for defining quiddity is considered invalid due to tahsil al-hasil?
A) Defining by itself
B) Defining by accidents
C) Defining by some parts
D) Defining by all parts

Key Takeaway
Defining a quiddity by itself or its parts leads to logical fallacies; only formal definition using special properties can provide distinction.

The Possibility of Formal Definition and Arrangement of Parts
Refining the impossibility conclusion: arrangement of parts and utility of formal definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the arrangement of parts avoids the fallacy of tahsil al-hasil and identify the two purposes of definition.

Core Idea
Proper arrangement of parts produces new knowledge; formal definition serves distinction, not essence.

The author responds to the objection that real definition is impossible by showing that the composite of arranged parts was not previously known. He also clarifies that formal definition serves the purpose of distinguishing the quiddity, even if it does not convey its essence.

Guided Path
1
Understand the detailed answer
Read the part starting from 'تفصيل الجواب' where the author explains how arrangement of parts produces new knowledge.
2
Analyze the arrangement process
See how the conceptualizations of individual parts, when arranged with the general preceding the specific and restricted, create a composite that was not known before.
3
Identify the two purposes of definition
The passage states that definition can aim for essence or for distinction. Real definition aims for essence, formal definition for distinction.
4
Evaluate the conclusion
Understand that real definition is impossible if taken as conveying the essence directly, but formal definition is possible and useful for discrimination.

وهو تحصيل الحاصل وأما التعريف الرسمي الذي يكون بالعوارض، فلا تتحصل به الحقيقة، نعم يمكن به بالتعريف الرسمى امتياز الحقيقة عنما عداها إذا كان بالخواص دون العرض العام .
ووجه لزوم تحصيل الحاصل بالتعريف أن تعريف ماهية من الماهيات أو حقيقة من الحقائق ( فإن الماهية هي الحقيقة بعد وقوعها في جواب السؤال بـ ( ما هي ؟ ) لا يخلو عن أحد من الاحتمالات الأربعة :
إما أن يكون تعريفها بنفسها، وإما أن يكون بجميع أجزائها، وإما أن يكون ببعض أجزائها، أو يكون بعوارضها، والكل باطل .
-١ أما بطلان الشق الأول، فإنّ تعريف الشيئ بنفسه تحصيل الحاصل، أي تحصيل الشيئ الذى كان حاصلاً من قبل، وهذا الغو، وأيضاً يلزم تقدم الشيئ (من حيث أنه معزف بالكسر ) على نفسه من حيث أنه معرّف بالفتح ) فإن الحد يكون مقدماً على المحدود.
۲ وأما الشق الثاني، فلأن جميع الأجزاء هو نفس الشيئ تفصيلاً، فيكون التعريف بها هو التعريف بنفس الشيئ مع لزوم المحال فيه أيضاً (وهو تقدم الشيئ على نفسه وتقدم الأجزاء على الكل.
-٣- وأما الشق الثالث، فلأن الكل (جميع الأجزاء) إذا لم يفد المعرفة، بل يلزم فيه تقدم الشيئ على نفسه، وتقدم الأجزاء كلاً أو بعضاً على الكل ممنوع، فكيف التعريف ببعض الأجزاء؟
-٤- وأما الشق الرابع ، ( وهو التعريف بالعوارض)، فإنه لا يمكن معرفة الحقيقة بالعوارض الخارجة عنها، فإنها لا تفيد علم الحقيقة، نعم يحصل بها امتياز الحقيقة عن جميع ما عداها إذا كانت العوارض من الخواص، وإلا فلا، فثبت أن تعريف الماهية (الحقيقة) غير ممكن بالتعريف الحقيقي ولا بالرسمى
تفصيل الجواب : أن التصورات المتعلقة بالأجزاء، أي أجزاء الحد تفصيلاً مثل تصور الحيوان، وتصور الناطق في تعريف الإنسان أو تصور اللفظ والوضع والمعنى والإفراد في تعريف الكلمة، إذا رتبت بتقدم العام على الخاص، وقيدت بجعل الخاص صفة للعام، حتى يحصل المركب التقييدى، فهذا المجموع المرتب المقيد (سواء كان له جزآن أو أكثر ) هو الحد الموصل إلى الصورة الواحدانية التى حصلت للحد ( بعد الهيئة التركيبية) وتعلقت بجميع أجزاء الحد اجمالاً، وهو أي مجموع الصور المتعلقة بأجزاء الحد، والتى عرضت لها الصورة الوحدانية بعد الترتيب والتركيب المحدود، وهذا المجموع المرتب المركب لم يكن حاصلاً من قبل فههنا أي في محلّ التعريف الحقيقى) تحصيل أمر (وهو العلم بالمجموع ) لم يكن حاصلاً قبل هذا الترتيب والتقييد والتركيب .
فتدبر : فيه إشارة إلى جواب آخر، وهو أن منع التعريف للماهية باعتبار العوارض ممنوع ؛ لأن الغرض من تعريف الماهية قد يكون تحصيل حقيقتها، ولاشك أن هذا الغرض لا يحصل من التعريف بالعوارض ؛ إذ لا تحصل الحقيقة بها ؛ وقد يكون الغرض من تعريفها امتيازها عن جميع ما عداها وهذا الغرض يحصل من التعريف بالرسم (بالعوارض) فالحكم بمنع التعريف الحقيقي حداً ورسماً ممنوع بهذا السند المذكور.
And it is attainment of the obtained. As for the formal definition (rasmi) which is by accidents, the essence is not attained by it. Yes, by formal definition it is possible to distinguish the essence from what is other than it if it is by special properties (khawass) and not by common accident. The reason for the necessity of attainment of the obtained by definition is that defining a quiddity among quiddities or a reality among realities (for quiddity is reality after it occurs in answer to the question 'what is it?') is not free from one of four possibilities: either it is defined by itself, or by all its parts, or by some of its parts, or by its accidents. All are invalid. As for the invalidity of the first branch: defining a thing by itself is attainment of the obtained, i.e., attaining something that was already obtained, and this is futile. Also, it requires the priority of the thing (as definiendum) over itself (as definition) for the definition precedes the defined. As for the second branch: because all parts are the thing itself in detail, so defining by them is defining by the thing itself, along with the impossibility also involved (priority of the thing over itself and priority of parts over the whole). As for the third branch: because the whole (all parts) if it does not give knowledge, rather there is in it priority of the thing over itself and priority of parts, whole or some, over the whole is prevented, so how can defining by some parts be? As for the fourth branch (definition by accidents): it is impossible to know the reality by accidents external to it, for they do not give knowledge of the reality. Yes, by them distinction of the reality from all others is obtained if the accidents are special properties; otherwise no. So it is established that defining quiddity (reality) is not possible by real definition nor by formal definition. Detailed answer: the conceptualizations related to the parts, i.e., the parts of the limit in detail, such as the conceptualization of animal and the conceptualization of rational in the definition of human, or the conceptualization of word, meaning, and singularity in the definition of kalima, when arranged with the general preceding the specific, and restricted by making the specific a description of the general, until the restrictive compound is obtained, then this arranged restricted composite (whether it has two parts or more) is the limit that leads to the unitary form that occurs to the limit (after the composite structure) and is related to all parts of the limit in summary. And it, i.e., the set of forms related to the parts of the limit, which are subject to the unitary form after arrangement and composition of the defined, was not obtained before. So here (in the place of real definition) there is attainment of something (knowledge of the composite) that was not obtained before this arrangement, restriction, and composition. So reflect: in it there is an indication of another answer, which is that the prevention of definition of quiddity by accidents is prevented; because the purpose of defining quiddity may be to attain its reality, and there is no doubt that this purpose is not obtained from definition by accidents, since reality is not attained by them; and the purpose of defining it may be to distinguish it from all others, and this purpose is obtained from definition by drawing (by accidents). So the judgment that real definition is prevented, both by essential and formal definition, is prevented by this mentioned chain.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of the definition of quiddity (mahiyyah) in the context of Islamic epistemology and usul al-fiqh. The author first distinguishes between real definition (ta'rif haqiqi) which aims to convey the essence, and formal definition (ta'rif rasmi) which uses accidents to distinguish the thing. He then presents four possible ways to define a quiddity: by itself, by all its parts, by some parts, or by accidents. Each is shown to be problematic. The first three involve circularity or infinite regress (tahsil al-hasil). The fourth, using accidents, cannot convey the essence itself but can provide distinction if the accidents are special properties (khawass). The author then provides a refined answer: the conceptualizations of the parts, when arranged properly, produce a composite that was not previously known, thus avoiding circularity. Finally, he notes that even definition by accidents is not entirely useless; it serves the purpose of distinction. This discussion is foundational for understanding how scholars define legal terms in usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
تعريف حقيقي (ta'rif haqiqi): Definition that conveys the essence of a thing through its essential parts.
تعريف رسمي (ta'rif rasmi): Definition that distinguishes a thing through its accidents or properties, without conveying the essence.
تحصيل الحاصل (tahsil al-hasil): Logical fallacy of achieving what is already achieved, i.e., circular definition.
ماهية (mahiyyah): Quiddity; the essence of a thing, what it is in answer to 'what is it?'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the detailed answer, how does arrangement of parts avoid the fallacy of tahsil al-hasil?
A) By using a different definition
B) By making the composite something that was not previously known
C) By using accidents instead of parts
D) By defining by itself

Key Takeaway
Real definition through proper arrangement yields new knowledge; formal definition serves the purpose of distinction.

Defining Daleel and Its Types
Introducing the fifth principle defining daleel and distinguishing qat'i from zanni

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define daleel (evidence) in Hanafi usul and distinguish it from amarah (probabilistic evidence).

Core Idea
Daleel leads to certainty; amarah gives only preponderance — the epistemological weight matters in deriving rulings.

Having completed the discussion on conceptual knowledge (tasawwur) through definitions, the author now turns to assertive knowledge (tasdiq) through proofs. This passage introduces the fifth principle, defining the term daleel (evidence) and explaining its relationship with the probabilistic evidence called amarah. Understanding this distinction is foundational for weighing different types of legal proof in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Locate the formal definition
Find the definition of daleel in the passage: it is that by which, through correct reflection (nazar sahih), one can arrive at a desired report (matlub khabari). This is a tool for reaching knowledge of a proposition.
The definition emphasizes the condition of correct reflection, not any random reasoning.
2
Identify the condition of correctness
The phrase 'correct reflection' (nazar sahih) indicates that the evidence must be used properly; incorrect reflection may lead to error even with sound evidence.
3
Examine the given example
The example is a logical syllogism: 'The world is changing, everything changing is contingent, so the world is contingent.' The third statement is the desired report. This illustrates the concept, not a fiqh ruling.
The example uses everyday observation, not scripture, to clarify the definition.
4
Distinguish between daleel and amarah
The passage notes that daleel may be restricted to definitive (qat'i) evidence, while probabilistic (zanni) evidence is called amarah. In Hanafi usul, this distinction affects the binding force of rulings derived from each type.
Some scholars use daleel broadly, but the Hanafi tradition often reserves it for qat'i.
5
Contextualize within the author's structure
The author places this after the discussion of conceptual knowledge (tasawwur), marking the transition to assertive knowledge (tasdiq). This signals the importance of evidence for confirming or denying legal claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ثم الدليل ما يمكن التوصل بصحيح النظر فيه إلى مطلوب خبری ک فالعالم حادث في قولنا : العالم متغيّر، وكل متغيّر حادث، فالعالم حادث، والثالث هو المطلوب (الخبرى وقد يخص (الدليل) بالقطعى ويسمّى (الدليل) الظني أمارة
و بعد الفراغ عن بيان الموصل التصورى وهو المعزف بالكسر ، والقول الشارح، شرع المصنف في بيان الموصل التصديقى وهو الدليل والحجة . -١ - تعريف الدليل وهو ما يمكن الوصول أي) وصول الذهن بالنظر الصحيح فيه ( في مدلوله) إلى مطلوب خبري (أي إلى العلم بمطلوب خبري )
The fifth principle on the definition of daleel (evidence) and explanation of its types and parts. Then daleel is that by which, through correct reflection in it, one can arrive at a desired report (khabari) such as 'the world is contingent' in our saying: the world is changing, and everything changing is contingent, so the world is contingent. The third is the desired (report). And (daleel) may be specified for definitive (qat'i) and the probabilistic (zanni) is called amarah (sign). And after finishing the explanation of the conceptual arriver (musil tasawwuri) which is the definition (mu'arraf bi-kasr) and the explicative statement (qawl sharh), the author began explaining the assertive arriver (musil tasdiqi) which is daleel and hujjah (proof). 1 - Definition of daleel: it is that by which the mind can reach, through correct reflection in it (on its meaning) to a desired report (i.e., to knowledge of a desired report).

Commentary
This passage marks the beginning of the fifth principle in the usul al-fiqh text. It defines the term daleel (evidence) as that which, through correct reflection (nazar sahih), leads to a desired report (matlub khabari), i.e., a proposition that is either true or false. The example given is the standard syllogism: the world is changing, everything changing is contingent, therefore the world is contingent. The third statement is the desired conclusion. The author then notes that daleel is sometimes restricted to definitive evidence (qat'i), while probabilistic evidence is called amarah (sign). This distinction is important in Hanafi usul for weighing different types of evidence. The passage also situates this discussion within the broader structure: having completed the discussion on conceptual knowledge (tasawwur) through definitions (mu'arraf), the author now moves to assertive knowledge (tasdiq) through proofs (daleel and hujjah).

Key Terms
دليل (daleel): That which, through correct reflection, leads to a desired report (knowledge of a claim).
أمارة (amarah): Probabilistic evidence that does not reach certainty.
مطلوب خبري (matlub khabari): A desired report or proposition that is either true or false.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Daleel is that which, through correct reflection, yields knowledge of a desired report; in Hanafi usul, it is often restricted to qat'i, while zanni evidence is called amarah.

The Validity of Definition by Accidents
Refuting the objection that definition through accidents cannot define essence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between hadd (essential definition) and rasm (descriptive definition) and state when definition through accidents (rasm) is valid in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Definition by accidents is valid when the goal is distinction, not essence.

In Hanafi usul, a proper definition (ta'rīf) can serve different purposes. Some scholars object that defining an essence through accidental properties (rasm) is invalid because it does not convey the true reality. This passage refutes that objection by clarifying that rasm is perfectly acceptable when the aim is merely to distinguish the thing from others. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying definitions in fiqh and usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
The opponent argues that definition through accidents (عوارض) cannot define an essence (ماهية) because accidents do not constitute the reality.
This is a common methodological objection.
2
Understand the Two Purposes of Definition
The author explains that definition can have two aims: (1) to acquire the true reality of the thing, or (2) to merely distinguish it from everything else.
The first aim requires hadd (essential definition), the second can be achieved by rasm (descriptive definition).
3
Apply the Distinction to the Objection
If the purpose is to acquire reality, the objection holds—rasm cannot do that. But if the purpose is mere distinction, rasm is sufficient and the objection is invalid.
Thus the objection is not universally valid; it depends on intent.
4
Recognize the Hanafi Rule on Definitions
The Hanafi position accepts both hadd and rasm as valid types of definition, each with its proper context. The key is that the validity of a definition is judged by its purpose.
This rule is applied whenever a definition is needed in fiqh or usul analysis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والإفراد في تعريف الكلمة، إذا رتبت بتقدم العام على الخاص، وقيدت بجعل الخاص صفة للعام، حتى يحصل المركب التقييدى، فهذا المجموع المرتب المقيد (سواء كان له جزآن أو أكثر ) هو الحد الموصل إلى الصورة الواحدانية التى حصلت للحد ( بعد الهيئة التركيبية) وتعلقت بجميع أجزاء الحد اجمالاً، وهو أي مجموع الصور المتعلقة بأجزاء الحد، والتى عرضت لها الصورة الوحدانية بعد الترتيب والتركيب المحدود، وهذا المجموع المرتب المركب لم يكن حاصلاً من قبل فههنا أي في محلّ التعريف الحقيقى) تحصيل أمر (وهو العلم بالمجموع ) لم يكن حاصلاً قبل هذا الترتيب والتقييد والتركيب .
فتدبر : فيه إشارة إلى جواب آخر، وهو أن منع التعريف للماهية باعتبار العوارض ممنوع ؛ لأن الغرض من تعريف الماهية قد يكون تحصيل حقيقتها، ولاشك أن هذا الغرض لا يحصل من التعريف بالعوارض ؛ إذ لا تحصل الحقيقة بها ؛ وقد يكون الغرض من تعريفها امتيازها عن جميع ما عداها وهذا الغرض يحصل من التعريف بالرسم (بالعوارض) فالحكم بمنع التعريف الحقيقي حداً ورسماً ممنوع بهذا السند المذكور.
And the individual parts in the definition of a word, when arranged by placing the general before the specific, and restricted by making the specific a qualification of the general, so that a restricted compound results, then this arranged restricted composite (whether it has two parts or more) is the definition that leads to the unitary image that occurred to the definition (after the compositional form) and attaches to all parts of the definition as a whole. And this composite of images attached to the parts of the definition, which acquired the unitary form after arrangement and composition, was not previously present. So here (in the place of true definition) there is an acquisition of something (knowledge of the composite) that was not present before this arrangement, restriction, and composition.
So ponder: there is an indication to another answer, which is that prohibiting the definition of an essence by considering accidents is prohibited because the purpose of defining an essence may be to acquire its reality, and undoubtedly this purpose is not obtained from definition by accidents, since reality is not obtained through them; and sometimes the purpose of defining it is its distinction from all else, and this purpose is obtained from definition by description (through accidents). So the judgment of prohibiting true definition, whether by essential definition or by description, is prohibited by this mentioned reasoning.

Commentary
This passage completes the discussion on definition (تعريف) by refuting an objection. The author addresses the argument that defining an essence (ماهية) through accidental features (عوارض) is invalid because it does not reveal the true reality. He explains that the purpose of definition is not always to convey the essence; sometimes it is only to distinguish the thing from others. In such cases, definition by description (رسم) using accidents is sufficient. This is a key methodological point in hanafi usul: the validity of definition depends on its purpose.

Key Terms
تعريف (ta'rīf): The act of defining a thing to make it known or distinct.
حد (ḥadd): An essential definition that conveys the true reality (quiddity) of a thing.
رسم (rasm): A descriptive definition that distinguishes a thing by its accidental properties.
عارض (ʿāriḍ): An accidental property that is not part of the essence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The validity of a definition depends on its purpose: hadd for essence, rasm for distinction.

Three Types of Disjunctive Exceptional Syllogism
Explaining the three subdivisions of disjunctive exceptional syllogism

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three types of disjunctive exceptional syllogism and determine which inferences (positing/negating) are valid for each.

Core Idea
The conclusion depends on whether disjuncts conflict in truth, falsehood, or both.

Disjunctive syllogisms are a key tool in Hanafi uṣūl al-fiqh for deriving rulings from exhaustive alternatives. This passage breaks down the three types of opposition between disjuncts—conflict in truth only, falsehood only, or both—and shows how each type dictates which inferences are logically valid. Mastering these distinctions sharpens your ability to evaluate arguments in juristic reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of opposition
Read the disjunctive statement and determine whether the two disjuncts conflict in truth, falsehood, or both. This is the key to the inference.
Conflict in truth only = man' al-jam'; conflict in falsehood only = man' al-khuluw; both = true disjunction.
2
Apply the valid inference pattern
For man' al-jam', positing one disjunct negates the other, but negating one does not affirm the other. For man' al-khuluw, negating one affirms the other, but positing one does not negate the other. For true disjunction, both directions are valid.
Memorize the asymmetry: the valid direction depends on which type of impossibility (jam' or khuluw) is prevented.
3
Test with the provided examples
Work through the stone/tree (man' al-jam'), not-animal/not-rational (man' al-khuluw), and even/odd (true disjunction) examples to see the reasoning in action.
Pay attention to why the reverse inference fails in the first two types.
4
Connect to uṣūl al-fiqh reasoning
Think of how a mujtahid uses such syllogisms to narrow down rulings when faced with exclusive options (e.g., a general text vs. a specific exception).
Example: If a ruling is either fard or wajib, and the evidence is not qat'i, then it cannot be fard (man' al-jam' type).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القياس الاستثنائى الانفصالي وأقسامه
ه الصورة الخامسة للقياس الاستثنائى المركب من المنفصلات وأشار المصنف إلى الأنواع الثلاثة من القياس الاستثنائى الانفصالي فقال: أن يعلم المنافاة بينهما (بين الأمرين) (۱) اما صدقا فقط، (٢) أو كذبا فقط ، (۳) أو فيهما (في الصدق والكذب معا) فيلزم النتائج بحسبها (أنواع المنافات) فتفكر
وإذا كان الحكم بين القضيتين بالانفصال والعناد بين الأمرين مع حرف الاستثناء فهو القياس الاستثنائى الانفصالي، ثم ذلك الانفصال والعناد لا يخلو عن الأنواع الثلاثة:

۱ : فإن التنافي إذا كان في الصدق فقط ( و يقال لها المنفصلة مانعة الجمع) ينتج وضع كل من المقدم والتالى رفع الآخر، نحو قوله اما أن يكون هذا حجراً أو شجراً، لكنه شجر، فلا يكون حجراً، وإلا لزم صدقهما معاً، وهي مانعة الجمع، ولا ينتج رفع كل وضع الآخر، لجواز الخلو عنهما، نحو إما أن يكون هذا شجراً أو حجراً، لكنه ليس بحجر، ولا يمكن أن تكون النتيجة فيكون شجراً، لجواز أن يكون مشار إليه (هذا) غيرهما .
٢: وإذا كانت المنافاة في الكذب فقط (وهي المنفصلة مانعة الخلو) ينتج رفع كلّ : (من المقدمتين) وضع الآخر نحو قوله اما أن يكون هذا الشيئ لا إنساناً أو يكون لا ناطقاً، لكنه لا ناطق فلا يكون إنساناً، أو لكنه إنسان، فلا يكون لا ناطقاً . :وقوله: فتفكر فيه إشارة إلى توجه القارئ إلى نتيجة كل من أنواع المنفصلة، والى أنواع نتائجها حسب الشرائط المعتبرة فيها .
وإلا لزم كذبهما معاً، ولا ينتج وضع كلّ رفع الآخر، لجواز اجتماعهما في الصدق، وكذا قولهم اما أن يكون الإنسان في البحر واما ان يكون لا يغرق .
٣: وإذا كانت في الصدق والكذب معاً (وهي المنفصلة الحقيقية ينتج وضع كل رفع الآخر، ورفع كلّ وضع الآخر كقولنا اما أن يكون هذا العدد زوجاً أو فرداً، لكنه زوج فلا يكون فرداً، أو لكنه ليس بفرد، فيكون زوجاً، لامتناع جمع الصدق والكذب معاً، وامتناع خلوهما .
فقد انتهت الصور الخمس للقياس ثلاث للاقتراني) واثنتان للاستثنائي الاتصالي والانفصالي .
وبانتهاء الصور الخمس انتهت المبادئ الخمسة المنطقية، وسيبدأ المصنف في بيان المبدئين الكلامين ان شاء الله
The exceptional disjunctive syllogism and its divisions. This is the fifth form of the exceptional syllogism composed of disjuncts. The author pointed to the three types of exceptional disjunctive syllogism, saying: One knows the opposition between them (the two matters) either (1) in truth only, (2) or in falsehood only, (3) or in both (in truth and falsehood together). So the conclusions follow according to them (the types of opposition). So reflect. And when the judgment between the two propositions is by disjunction and opposition between the two matters with the particle of exception, then it is the exceptional disjunctive syllogism. Then that disjunction and opposition does not escape from the three types: 1: For if the opposition is in truth only (called the disjunction that prevents conjunction), it yields: positing each of the antecedent and consequent entails negating the other. Example: 'This is either a stone or a tree, but it is a tree, so it is not a stone'; otherwise both would be true together. This is the preventing-conjunction disjunction. And it does not yield: negating each entails positing the other, because of the possibility of both being absent. Example: 'This is either a tree or a stone, but it is not a stone'; the result cannot be that it is a tree, because it is possible that the referent (this) is something else. 2: And if the opposition is in falsehood only (called the disjunction that prevents emptiness), it yields: negating each (of the two premises) entails positing the other. Example: 'This thing is either not-animal or not-rational, but it is not-rational, so it is not an animal'; or 'but it is an animal, so it is not not-rational.' And his saying: 'so reflect' points to the reader's attention to the result of each type of disjunction, and to the types of its results according to the conditions considered in them. Otherwise both would be false together. And it does not yield: positing each entails negating the other, because of the possibility of both being true. Similarly their saying: 'The human is either in the sea or not drowning.' 3: And if it is in truth and falsehood together (called the true disjunction), it yields: positing each entails negating the other, and negating each entails positing the other. Example: 'This number is either even or odd, but it is even, so it is not odd'; or 'but it is not odd, so it is even.' Because of the impossibility of both truth and falsehood together, and the impossibility of their absence. Thus the five forms of syllogism have ended: three for the conjunctive and two for the exceptional, both conditional and disjunctive. And with the end of the five forms, the five logical principles have ended, and the author will begin to explain the two theological principles, God willing.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the three types of disjunctive exceptional syllogism (al-qiyas al-istithnā'ī al-infiṣālī). The author, after stating the general rule, lists the three types based on the nature of opposition (tanāfi) between the two disjuncts. The first type, man' al-jam' (preventing conjunction), applies when the disjuncts cannot both be true. In such a case, affirming one requires negating the other, but negating one does not allow affirming the other because both could be false. The example given is 'stone or tree': if it is a tree, it is not a stone; but if it is not a stone, it could still be something else like a book. The second type, man' al-khuluww (preventing emptiness), applies when the disjuncts cannot both be false, i.e., at least one must be true. Here, negating one implies affirming the other, but affirming one does not negate the other because both could be true. The example illustrates with 'not-animal or not-rational': if it is not rational, then it cannot be an animal (since all animals are rational). The third type, al-munfaṣila al-ḥaqīqiyya (true disjunction), applies when the disjuncts are mutually exclusive and exhaustive: they cannot both be true nor both false. Thus, affirming one negates the other, and negating one affirms the other, as in 'even or odd'. This logical classification is foundational for Hanafi uṣūl al-fiqh because analogical reasoning (qiyās) often relies on conditional and disjunctive syllogisms to derive rulings. The author concludes by noting that this completes the five logical principles, after which he will move to kalām principles.

Key Terms
المنفصلة مانعة الجمع (al-munfaṣila māni'at al-jam'): A disjunction where the two disjuncts cannot both be true, but may both be false.
المنفصلة مانعة الخلو (al-munfaṣila māni'at al-khuluw): A disjunction where the two disjuncts cannot both be false, but may both be true.
المنفصلة الحقيقية (al-munfaṣila al-ḥaqīqiyya): A disjunction where the two disjuncts cannot both be true nor both false, i.e., perfectly exclusive and exhaustive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of disjunctive syllogism allows both disjuncts to be true simultaneously?
A) Preventing conjunction (man' al-jam')
B) Preventing emptiness (man' al-khuluw)
C) True disjunction (al-munfaṣila al-ḥaqīqiyya)
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
The conclusion a disjunctive syllogism yields depends on whether the disjuncts conflict in truth, falsehood, or both.
